<@01>The Morning Prayers
<@01>תפלת שחרית
<@02>Upon Arising in the Morning
<@02>סדר השכמת הבוקר
<M in>Upon waking in the morning, even before washing your hands, say:<FC>
<M t2>I give thanks to You
<M h> מוֹדֶה אֲנִי לְפָנֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>living and everlasting King
<M h> מֶֽלֶךְ חַי וְקַיָּם <FL>
<M e>for You have restored my soul with mercy.
<M h> שֶׁהֶחֱזַֽרְתָּ בִּי נִשְׁ֒מָתִי בְּחֶמְלָה, <FL>
<M e>Great is Your faithfulness.
<M h> רַבָּה אֱמוּנָתֶֽךָ: <FL>
<M in>After washing your hands, say:<FC>
<M t2>The beginning of wisdom is fear of Adonoy,
<M h> רֵאשִׁית חָכְמָה יִרְאַת יְהֹוָה, <FL>
<M e>good understanding
<M h> שֵֽׂכֶל טוֹב <FL>
<M e>to all who perform [His commandments],
<M h> לְכָל עֹשֵׂיהֶם, <FL>
<M e>His praise endures forever.
<M h> תְּהִלָּתוֹ עוֹמֶֽדֶת לָעַד: <FL>
<M e>Blessed [is His] Name,
<M h> בָּרוּךְ שֵׁם
<M e>Whose glorious kingdom
<M h> כְּבוֹד מַלְכוּתוֹ <FL>
<M e>is forever and ever.
<M h> לְעוֹלָם וָעֶד: <FL>
<M in>Before putting on your </i>tallis katan<i> say:<FC>
<M t2>Blessed are You, Adonoy
<M h> <M newbold> בָּרוּךְ <M reg> אַתָּה יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>our God, King of the Universe
<M h> אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ מֶֽלֶךְ הָעוֹלָם <FL>
<M e>Who sanctified us with His commandments
<M h> אֲשֶׁר קִדְּ֒שָֽׁנוּ בְּמִצְוֹתָיו <FL>
<M e>and commanded us
<M h> וְצִוּנוּ <FL>
<M e>concerning the <i>mitzva</i> of <i>tzitzis</i> (fringes).
<M h> עַל מִצְוַת צִיצִית: <FL>
<M tex><M t1>May it be Your will
<M h> יְהִי רָצוֹן מִלְּ֒פָנֶיךָ <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, my God, and God of my fathers,
<M h> יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהַי וֵאלֹהֵי אֲבוֹתַי <FL>
<M e>to consider [my fulfillment of]
<M h> שֶׁתְּ֒הֵא חֲשׁוּבָה <FL>
<M e>the <i>mitzva</i> of <i>tzitzis</i> before You
<M h> מִצְוַת צִיצִית לְפָנֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>as though I had fulfilled it
<M h> כְּאִלּוּ קִיַּמְתִּֽיהָ <FL>
<M e>in every detail,
<M h> בְּכָל פְּרָטֶֽיהָ <FL>
<M e>accurately and with full intent,
<M h> וְדִקְדּוּקֶֽיהָ וְכַוּנוֹתֶֽיהָ <FL>
<M e>and the 613<M tnt> commandments
<M h> וְתַרְיַ"ג מִצְווֹת
<M e>that depend on it.
<M h> הַתְּ֒לוּיוֹת בָּהּ, <FL>
<M e>Amein, Selah.
<M h> אָמֵן סֶלָה: <FL>
<@02>Putting On the Tallis
<@02>סדר עטיפת טלית
<M in>While examining the fringes of the </i>tallis<i> say:<FC>
<M t2>My soul, bless Adonoy,
<M h> <M newbold> בָּרְ֒כִי נַפְשִׁי <M reg> אֶת-יְהֹוָה, <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, my God, You are greatly exalted.
<M h> יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהַי גָּדַֽלְתָּ מְאֹד, <FL>
<M e>With beauty and splendor
<M h> הוֹד וְהָדָר <FL>
<M e>are You clothed
<M h> לָבָֽשְׁתָּ: <FL>
<M e>enwrapped in light, garment-like;
<M h> עֹֽטֶה-אוֹר כַּשַּׂלְמָה, <FL>
<M e>You spread out the heavens like a curtain.<M tnt>
<M h> נוֹטֶה שָׁמַֽיִם כַּיְ֒רִיעָה: <FL>
<M long> לְשֵׁם יִחוּד קוּדְ֒שָׁא בְּרִיךְ הוּא וּשְׁ֒כִינְתֵּהּ, בִּדְ֒חִילוּ וּרְ֒חִימוּ לְיַחֵד שֵׁם י"ה בו"ה בְּיִחוּדָא שְׁלִים בְּשֵׁם כָּל יִשְׂרָאֵל, הֲרֵינִי מִתְעַטֵּף גּוּפִי בַּצִּיצִית, כֵּן תִּתְעַטֵּף <fj>
<xx> <M tex> <M long> נִשְׁ֒מָתִי וּרְ֒מַ"ח אֵיבָרַי וּשְׁסָ"ה גִידַי בְּאוֹר הַצִּיצִית הָעוֹלֶה תַּרְיַ"ג, וּכְ֒שֵׁם שֶׁאֲנִי מִתְכַּסֶּה בַּטַּלִּית בָּעוֹלָם הַזֶּה כַּךְ אֶזְכֶּה לַחֲלוּקָא דְרַבָּנָן וּלְ֒טַלִּית נָאָה לָעוֹלָם הַבָּא בְּגַן עֵֽדֶן, וְעַל יְדֵי מִצְוַת צִיצִית, תִּנָּצֵל נַפְשִׁי רוּחִי וְנִשְׁ֒מָתִי וּתְ֒פִלָּתִי מִן הַחִיצוֹנִים, וְהַטַּלִּית יִפְרֹשׂ כְּנָפָיו עֲלֵיהֶם, וְיַצִּילֵם כְּנֶֽשֶׁר יָעִיר קִנּוֹ עַל גּוֹזָלָיו יְרַחֵף, וּתְ֒הֵא חֲשׁוּבָה מִצְוַת צִיצִית לִפְ֒נֵי הַקָּדוֹשׁ בָּרוּךְ הוּא, כְּאִלּוּ קִיַּמְתִּֽיהָ בְּכָל פְּרָטֶֽיהָ, וְדִקְדּוּקֶֽיהָ, וְכַוּנוֹתֶֽיהָ, וְתַרְיַ"ג מִצְווֹת הַתְּ֒לוּיוֹת בָּהּ, אָמֵן סֶֽלָה: <FC>
<M t1>Blessed are You, Adonoy
<M h> בָּרוּךְ אַתָּה יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>our God, King of the Universe,
<M h> אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ מֶֽלֶךְ הָעוֹלָם <FL>
<M e>Who sanctified us with(His commandments
<M h> אֲשֶׁר קִדְּ֒שָֽׁנוּ בְּמִצְוֹתָיו <FL>
<M e>and commanded us
<M h> וְצִוּנוּ <FL>
<M e>to enwrap ourselves with <i>tzitzis.</i>
<M h> לְהִתְעַטֵּף בַּצִּיצִית: <FL>
<M in>Cover your head with the </i>tallis<i> and say:<FC>
<M t2>How precious is Your kindness, God;
<M h> מַה יָּקָר חַסְ֒דְּךָ אֱלֹהִים <FL>
<M e>the children of men
<M h> וּבְ֒נֵי אָדָם <FL>
<M e>take refuge in the shadow of Your wings.
<M h> בְּצֵל כְּנָפֶֽיךָ יֶחֱסָֽיוּן: <FL>
<M e>They will be filled
<M h> יִרְוְיֻן <FL>
<M e>from the abundance of Your House,
<M h> מִדֶּֽשֶׁן בֵּיתֶֽךָ <FL>
<M e>and from the stream of Your delights
<M h> וְנַֽחַל עֲדָנֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>You will give them to drink.
<M h> תַשְׁקֵם: <FL>
<M e>For with You is the source of life,
<M h> כִּי-עִמְּ֒ךָ מְקוֹר חַיִּים, <FL>
<M e>in Your light shall we see light.
<M h> בְּאוֹרְ֒ךָ נִרְאֶה-אוֹר: <FL>
<M e>Extend Your kindness
<M h> מְשֹׁךְ חַסְדְּךָ
<M e>to those who know You,
<M h> לְיֹדְ֒עֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>and Your righteousness
<M h> וְצִדְ֒קָתְ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>to the upright in heart.<M tnt>
<M h> לְיִשְׁ֒רֵי-לֵב: <FL>
<@02>Putting on the Tefillin
<@02>סדר הנחת תפלין
<M long> </b> לְשֵׁם יִחוּד קוּדְ֒שָׁא בְּרִיךְ הוּא וּשְׁ֒כִינְתֵּהּ בִּדְ֒חִילוּ וּרְ֒חִימוּ, לְיַחֵד שֵׁם י"ה בו"ה בְּיִחוּדָא שְׁלִים בְּשֵׁם כָּל יִשְׂרָאֵל, הִנְּנִי מְכַוּן בַּהֲנָחַת תְּפִלִּין לְקַיֵּם מִצְוַת בּוֹרְ֒אִי, שֶׁצִּוּנוּ לְהָנִֽיחַ תְּפִלִּין כַּכָּתוּב בְּתוֹרָתוֹ וּקְ֒שַׁרְתָּם לְאוֹת עַל יָדֶֽךָ, וְהָיוּ לְטֹטָפֹת בֵּין עֵינֶֽיךָ, וְהֵם אַרְבַּע פַּרְשִׁיּוֹת אֵֽלּוּ, שְׁמַע. וְהָיָה אִם שָׁמֹֽעַ. קַדֶּשׁ. וְהָיָה כִי-יְבִאֲךָ. שֶׁיֵּשׁ בָּהֶם יִחוּדוֹ וְאַחְדּוּתוֹ יִתְבָּרַךְ שְׁמוֹ בָּעוֹלָם, וְשֶׁנִּזְכֹּר נִסִּים וְנִפְלָאוֹת, שֶׁעָשָׂה עִמָּֽנוּ בְּהוֹצִיאוֹ אוֹתָֽנוּ מִמִּצְרָֽיִם, וַאֲשֶׁר לוֹ הַכֹּֽחַ וְהַמֶּמְשָׁלָה בָּעֶלְיוֹנִים וּבַתַּחְתּוֹנִים לַעֲשׂוֹת בָּהֶם כִּרְ֒צוֹנוֹ, וְצִוּנוּ לְהָנִיחַ עַל הַיָּד, לְזִכְרוֹן זְרֽוֹעַ הַנְּ֒טוּיָה. וְשֶׁהִיא נֶֽגֶד הַלֵּב לְשַׁעְבֵּד בָּזֶה תַּאֲוַת וּמַחְשְׁבוֹת לִבֵּֽנוּ לַעֲבוֹדָתוֹ יִתְבָּרַךְ שְׁמוֹ, וְעַל הָרֹאשׁ נֶֽגֶד הַמּֽוֹחַ, שֶׁהַנְּ֒שָׁמָה שֶׁבְּ֒מוֹחִי עִם שְׁאָר חוּשַׁי וְכֹחוֹתַי כֻּלָּם יִהְיוּ מְשֻׁעְבָּדִים לַעֲבוֹדָתוֹ יִתְבָּרַךְ שְׁמוֹ, וּמִשֶּֽׁפַע מִצְוַת תְּפִלִּין יִתְמַשֵּׁךְ עָלַי לִהְיוֹת לִי חַיִּים אֲרֻכִּים, וְשֶֽׁפַע קֹֽדֶשׁ, וּמַחֲשָׁבוֹת קְדוֹשׁוֹת, בְּלִי הִרְהוּר חֵטְא וְעָוֹן כְּלָל וְשֶׁלֹּא יְפַתֵּֽנוּ וְלֹא יִתְגָּֽרֶה-בָּֽנוּ יֵֽצֶר הָרָע, וְיַנִּיחֵֽנוּ לַעֲבֹד אֶת יְהֹוָה, כַּאֲשֶׁר עִם לְבָבֵֽנוּ, וִיהִי רָצוֹן מִלְּ֒פָנֶֽיךָ, יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ, וֵאלֹהֵי אֲבוֹתֵֽינוּ, שֶׁתְּ֒הֵא חֲשׁוּבָה מִצְוַת הֲנָחַת תְּפִלִּין, לִפְ֒נֵי הַקָּדוֹשׁ בָּרוּךְ הוּא, כְּאִלּוּ קִיַּמְתִּֽיהָ בְּכָל פְּרָטֶֽיהָ וְדִקְדּוּקֶֽיהָ, וְכַוּנוֹתֶֽיהָ, וְתַרְיַ"ג מִצְווֹת הַתְּ֒לוּיוֹת בָּהּ, אָמֵן סֶֽלָה: <FC>
<M in>Place the "tefillin of the arm" on the muscle of your left arm, and before tightening it, say:<FC>
<M t2>Blessed are You, Adonoy
<M h> <M newbold> בָּרוּךְ <M reg> אַתָּה יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>our God, King of the Universe,
<M h> אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ מֶֽלֶךְ הָעוֹלָם <FL>
<M tex><M e>Who sanctified us with His commandments
<M h> אֲשֶׁר קִדְּ֒שָֽׁנוּ בְּמִצְוֹתָיו <FL>
<M e>and commanded us to put on <i>tefillin.</i>
<M h> וְצִוּנוּ לְהָנִיחַ תְּפִלִּין: <FL>
<M in>Wrap the strap around your arm 7 times and then place the "tefillin of the head" on your head above the region between your eyes, and say:<FC>
<M t2>Blessed are You, Adonoy
<M h> <M newbold> בָּרוּךְ <M reg> אַתָּה יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>our God, King of the Universe,
<M h> אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ מֶֽלֶךְ הָעוֹלָם <FL>
<M e>Who sanctified us with His commandments,
<M h> אֲשֶׁר קִדְּ֒שָֽׁנוּ בְּמִצְוֹתָיו <FL>
<M e>and commanded us
<M h> וְצִוּנוּ <FL>
<M e>concerning the <i>mitzvoh</i> of <i>tefillin.</i>
<M h> עַל מִצְוַת תְּפִלִּין: <FL>
<M in>Then say immediately:<FC>
<M t2>Blessed [is His] Name, Whose glorious kingdom
<M h> בָּרוּךְ שֵׁם כְּבוֹד מַלְ֒כוּתוֹ <FL>
<M e>is forever and ever.
<M h> לְעוֹלָם וָעֶד: <FL>
<M in>With the "tefillin of the head" in place, say:<FC>
<M t2>And from Your wisdom, most high Almighty,
<M h> <M newbold> וּמֵחָכְמָתְ֒ךָ <M reg> אֵל עֶלְיוֹן <FL>
<M e>may You impart to me;
<M h> תַּאֲצִיל עָלַי <FL>
<M e>and from Your understanding,
<M h> וּמִבִּינָתְ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>give me understanding.
<M h> תְּבִינֵֽנִי <FL>
<M e>With Your lovingkindness,
<M h> וּבְ֒חַסְדְּךָ <FL>
<M e>do great things with me.
<M h> תַּגְדִּיל עָלַי <FL>
<M e>With Your merit,
<M h> וּבִגְ֒בוּרָתְ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>cut off my enemies and opponents.
<M h> תַּצְמִית אוֹיְ֒בַי וְקָמַי <FL>
<M e>Pour bountiful oil
<M h> וְשֶׁמֶן הַטּוֹב תָּרִיק <FL>
<M e>upon the seven branches of the menorah,
<M h> עַל שִׁבְעָה קְנֵי הַמְּ֒נוֹרָה <FL>
<M e>in order to cause goodness
<M h> לְהַשְׁפִּֽיעַ טוּבְ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>to flow to Your creatures.
<M h> לִבְ֒רִיּוֹתֶֽיךָ: <FL>
<M e>Open Your hand
<M h> פּוֹתֵחַ אֶת יָדֶֽךָ <FL>
<M e>and satisfy the desire of every living thing.
<M h> וּמַשְׂבִּֽיעַ לְכָל חַי רָצוֹן: <FL>
<M in>When wrapping the strap around the middle finger of your left hand, say:<FC>
<M t2>And I will betrothe you to me forever;
<M h> <M newbold> וְאֵרַשְׂתִּיךְ <M reg> לִי לְעוֹלָם, <FL>
<M e>and I will betrothe you to me
<M h> וְאֵרַשְׂתִּיךְ לִי
<M tex><M e>in righteousness,
<M h> בְּצֶֽדֶק <FL>
<M e>in justice, in kindliness, and in mercy.
<M h> וּבְ֒מִשְׁפָּט וּבְ֒חֶֽסֶד וּבְ֒רַחֲמִים: <FL>
<M e>And I will betrothe you to me in faithfulness
<M h> וְאֵרַשְׂתִּיךְ לִי בֶּאֱמוּנָה, <FL>
<M e>and you shall know Adonoy.<M tnt>
<M h> וְיָדַֽעַתְּ אֶת-יְהֹוָה: <FL>
<M in>The following chapters, found in Exodus 13:1-16, are recited while wearing the tefillin, since they make direct reference to the mitzvah of tefillin.<FC>
<M long> וַיְ֒דַבֵּר <M reg> יְהֹוָה אֶל-משֶׁה לֵּאמֹר: קַדֶּשׁ-לִי כָל-בְּכוֹר פֶּֽטֶר כָּל-רֶֽחֶם בִּבְ֒נֵי יִשְׂרָאֵל בָּאָדָם וּבַבְּ֒הֵמָה לִי הוּא: וַיֹּֽאמֶר משֶׁה אֶל-הָעָם זָכוֹר אֶת-הַיּוֹם הַזֶּה אֲשֶׁר יְצָאתֶם מִמִּצְרַֽיִם מִבֵּית עֲבָדִים כִּי בְּחֹֽזֶק יָד הוֹצִיא יְהֹוָה אֶתְ֒כֶם מִזֶּה וְלֹא יֵאָכֵל חָמֵץ: הַיּוֹם אַתֶּם יֹצְ֒אִים בְּחֹֽדֶשׁ הָאָבִיב: וְהָיָה כִי-יְבִיאֲךָ יְהֹוָה אֶל-אֶֽרֶץ הַכְּ֒נַעֲנִי וְהַחִתִּי וְהָאֱמֹרִי וְהַחִוּי וְהַיְ֒בוּסִי אֲשֶׁר נִשְׁבַּע לַאֲבֹתֶֽיךָ לָֽתֶת לָךְ אֶֽרֶץ זָבַת חָלָב וּדְבָשׁ וְעָבַדְתָּ אֶת-הָעֲבֹדָה הַזֹּאת בַּחֹֽדֶשׁ הַזֶּה: שִׁבְעַת יָמִים תֹּאכַל מַצֹּת וּבַיּוֹם הַשְּׁ֒בִיעִי חַג לַיהוָֹה: מַצּוֹת יֵאָכֵל אֵת שִׁבְעַת הַיָּמִים וְלֹא-יֵרָאֶה לְךָ חָמֵץ וְלֹא-יֵרָאֶה לְךָ שְׂאֹר בְּכָל-גְּבֻלֶֽךָ: וְהִגַּדְתָּ לְבִנְ֒ךָ בַּיּוֹם הַהוּא לֵאמֹר בַּֽעֲבוּר זֶה עָשָׂה יְהֹוָה לִי בְּצֵאתִי מִמִּצְרָֽיִם: וְהָיָה לְךָ לְאוֹת עַל-יָדְ֒ךָ וּלְ֒זִכָּרוֹן בֵּין עֵינֶֽיךָ לְמַֽעַן תִּֽהְיֶה תּוֹרַת יְהֹוָה בְּפִֽיךָ כִּי בְּיָד חֲזָקָה הוֹצִאֲךָ יְהֹוָה מִמִּצְרָֽיִם: וְשָׁמַרְתָּ אֶת-הַחֻקָּה הַזֹּאת לְמוֹעֲדָהּ מִיָּמִים יָמִֽימָה: וְהָיָה כִּי-יְבִאֲךָ יְהֹוָה אֶל-אֶֽרֶץ הַכְּ֒נַעֲנִי כַּאֲשֶׁר נִשְׁבַּע לְךָ וְלַאֲבֹתֶֽיךָ וּנְ֒תָנָהּ לָךְ: וְהַעֲבַרְתָּ כָל-פֶּֽטֶר-רֶֽחֶם לַֽיהוָֹה וְכָל פֶּֽטֶר שֶֽׁגֶר בְּהֵמָה אֲשֶׁר יִהְיֶה לְךָ הַזְּ֒כָרִים לַיהוָֹה: וְכָל-פֶּֽטֶר חֲמֹר תִּפְדֶּה בְשֶׂה וְאִם-לֹא תִפְדֶּה וַעֲרַפְתּוֹ וְכֹל בְּכוֹר אָדָם בְּבָנֶֽיךָ תִּפְדֶּה: וְהָיָה כִּי-יִשְׁאָלְ֒ךָ בִנְ֒ךָ מָחָר לֵאמֹר מַה-זֹּאת וְאָמַרְתָּ אֵלָיו בְּחֹֽזֶק יָד הוֹצִיאָֽנוּ יְהֹוָה מִמִּצְרַֽיִם מִבֵּית עֲבָדִים: וַיְ֒הִי כִּי-הִקְשָׁה פַרְעֹה לְשַׁלְּ֒חֵנוּ וַיַּהֲרֹג יְהֹוָה כָּל-בְּכוֹר בְּאֶֽרֶץ מִצְרַֽיִם מִבְּֽ֒כֹר אָדָם וְעַד-בְּכוֹר בְּהֵמָה עַל-כֵּן אֲנִי זֹבֵֽחַ לַֽיהוָֹה כָּל-פֶּֽטֶר רֶֽחֶם הַזְּ֒כָרִים וְכָל-בְּכוֹר בָּנַי אֶפְדֶּה: וְהָיָה לְאוֹת עַל-יָדְ֒כָה וּלְ֒טוֹטָפֹת בֵּין עֵינֶֽיךָ כִּי בְּחֹֽזֶק יָד הוֹצִיאָֽנוּ יְהֹוָה מִמִּצְרָֽיִם: <FC>
<xx><M tex><M ex><EM><EN>Adonoy spoke to Moses, saying: "Sanctify unto me all the firstborn whatsoever opens the womb among the Children of Israel, both of man and beast is Mine." And Moses said to the people: "Remember this day on which you came out of Egypt, out of the house of bondage, for with a strong hand Adonoy brought you out from here, and [therefore] you must not eat <i>chametz.</i> This day you are departing, in the month of springtime. And it will be when Adonoy will bring you to the land of the Canaanites and the Hittites, and the Emorites, and the Hivites, and the Jebusites, which He swore to your fathers to give you, a land flowing with milk and honey, you shall perform this service in this month. Seven days, you shall eat matzos, and on the seventh day there shall be a festival [dedicated] to Adonoy. Matzos shall be eaten during these seven days, and no <i>chametz</i> and no leaven shall be seen in your possession within all your boundaries. And you shall relate to your son on that day, saying: ‘Because of this Adonoy acted on my behalf when I came out of Egypt. And it shall be for a sign upon your arm<M tnt> and for a reminder between your eyes<M tnt> so that Adonoy’s teaching will be [the words of] your mouth; for with a strong hand Adonoy brought you out of Egypt. And you shall keep this ordinance in its appointed time from year to year.<FL>
<EM><EN>And it will be, when Adonoy will bring you to the land of the Canaanites as He swore unto you and to your fathers, and will have given it to you. Then you shall bring to Adonoy every one that opens the womb, and every firstling that is dropped by cattle that belong to you, the males shall belong to Adonoy, The firstling of a donkey you shall redeem with a lamb; and if you do not redeem it, then you must kill it by breaking its neck. You must redeem every firstborn of man among your children. And it will be when your son asks you in future times, saying: ‘What is this?’ You shall say to him: ‘With a strong hand Adonoy brought us out of Egypt, out of the house of bondage. And it was when Pharaoh unyieldingly refused to let us go, that Adonoy killed all the firstborn in the land of Egypt, from the firstborn of man, to the firstborn of beast; therefore I sacrifice to Adonoy all that opens the womb that are males, and every firstborn of my sons, I redeem.’ And it shall be a sign upon your arm,<M tnt> and for <i>totafos</i> between your eyes,<M tnt> for with a strong hand, Adonoy brought us out of Egypt.<FL>
<@02>Ma Tovu
<@02>מה טובו
<M in>Before beginning the Morning Prayers you should say the following:<FC>
<M t2>I hereby accept upon myself
<M h> הֲרֵינִי מְקַבֵּל עָלַי <FL>
<M e>the positive commandment
<M h> מִצְוַת עֺשֵׂה שֶׁל <FL>
<M e>to love my fellow Jew.
<M h> וְאָהַבְתָּ לְרֵעֲךָ כָּמֽוֹךָ: <FL>
<M in><EM><EN>The following verses from Scriptures are recited upon entering the synagogue, as though asking permission of God to enter and pray in His Holy place.<FC>
<M t2>How good are your tents, Jacob:
<M h> <M newbold> מַה טֹּֽבוּ <M reg> אֹהָלֶֽיךָ יַעֲקֹב <FL>
<M e>your dwelling places, Israel.<M tnt>
<M h> מִשְׁכְּ֒נֹתֶֽיךָ יִשְׂרָאֵל: <FL>
<M e>As for me, through Your abundant kindness
<M h> וַאֲנִי בְּרֹב חַסְדְּ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>I will enter Your House;
<M h> אָבוֹא בֵיתֶֽךָ <FL>
<M e>I will prostrate myself
<M h> אֶשְׁתַּחֲוֶה <FL>
<M e>toward Your Holy Sanctuary in awe of You.<M tnt>
<M h> אֶל הֵיכַל-קָדְשְׁ֒ךָ בְּיִרְאָתֶֽךָ: <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, I love the Dwelling, Your House,
<M h> יְהֹוָה אָהַֽבְתִּי מְעוֹן בֵּיתֶֽךָ <FL>
<M e>and the place where Your glory resides.<M tnt>
<M h> וּמְ֒קוֹם מִשְׁכַּן כְּבוֹדֶֽךָ: <FL>
<M e>I will prostrate myself, and bow,
<M h> וַאֲנִי אֶשְׁתַּחֲוֶה וְאֶכְרָֽעָה <FL>
<M e>I will kneel<M tnt> before Adonoy, my Maker.
<M h> אֶבְרְכָה לִפְ֒נֵי יְהֹוָה עֹשִׂי: <FL>
<M e>May my prayer to You Adonoy
<M h> וַאֲנִי תְפִלָּתִי-לְךָ יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>be at a favorable time;
<M h> עֵת רָצוֹן <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>God, in the abundance of Your kindness
<M h> אֱלֹהִים בְּרָב-חַסְדֶּֽךָ <FL>
<M e>answer me
<M h> עֲנֵֽנִי
<M e>with the truth of Your deliverance.<M tnt>
<M h> בֶּאֱמֶת יִשְׁעֶֽךָ: <FL>
<@02>Adon Olam
<@02>אדון עולם
<M ex><EM><EN>This hymn has been attributed to R’ Shlomo ibn Gabirol who lived in Spain during the eleventh century. While praising God’s omnipotence and providence, it clarifies the meaning of the name Adonoy so that before proceeding to pray, each worshiper understands the significance of the God he is addressing.<FL>
<M t2>Master of the Universe Who reigned
<M h> <M newbold> אֲדוֹן עוֹלָם <M reg> אֲשֶׁר מָלַךְ, <FL>
<M e>before any creature was created.
<M h> בְּטֶֽרֶם כָּל יְצִיר נִבְרָא: <FL>
<M e>At the time when all was made by His will,
<M h> לְעֵת נַעֲשָׂה בְחֶפְצוֹ כֹּל, <FL>
<M e>then was His Name proclaimed King.
<M h> אֲזַי מֶֽלֶךְ שְׁמוֹ נִקְרָא: <FL>
<M e>And after all things shall cease to be
<M h> וְאַחֲרֵי כִּכְ֒לוֹת הַכֹּל, <FL>
<M e>the Awesome One will reign alone.
<M h> לְבַדּוֹ יִמְלֹךְ נוֹרָא: <FL>
<M e>He was, He is,
<M h> וְהוּא הָיָה וְהוּא הֹוֶה, <FL>
<M e>and He shall be in glory.
<M h> וְהוּא יִהְיֶה בְּתִפְאָרָה: <FL>
<M e>He is One, and there is no second
<M h> וְהוּא אֶחָד וְאֵין שֵׁנִי, <FL>
<M e>to compare to Him, to associate [with Him].
<M h> לְהַמְשִׁיל לוֹ לְהַחְבִּֽירָה: <FL>
<M e>Without beginning, without end,
<M h> בְּלִי רֵאשִׁית בְּלִי תַכְלִית, <FL>
<M e>power and dominion are His.
<M h> וְלוֹ הָעֹז וְהַמִּשְׂרָה: <FL>
<M e>He is my God and my ever-living Redeemer,
<M h> וְהוּא אֵלִי וְחַי גּוֹאֲלִי, <FL>
<M e>the Rock of my destiny in times of distress.
<M h> וְצוּר חֶבְלִי בְּעֵת צָרָה: <FL>
<M e>He is my flag<M tnt> and my refuge;
<M h> וְהוּא נִסִּי וּמָנוֹס לִי, <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>He is the portion of my cup on the day I call.<M tnt>
<M h> מְנָת כּוֹסִי בְּיוֹם אֶקְרָא: <FL>
<M e>Into His hand I entrust my spirit
<M h> בְּיָדוֹ אַפְקִיד רוּחִי, <FL>
<M e>[both] when I sleep and when I awaken.
<M h> בְּעֵת אִישַׁן וְאָעִֽירָה: <FL>
<M e>And with my spirit my body [too],
<M h> וְעִם רוּחִי גְּוִיָּתִי, <FL>
<M e>Adonoy is with me, I shall not fear.
<M h> יְהֹוָה לִי וְלֹא אִירָא: <FL>
<@02>Yigdal
<@02>יגדל
<M ex><EM><EN>This hymn, written by Daniel ben Yehuda, who was a Dayan in Rome about 1300, is based on Maimonides’ 13 principles of Judaism. According to Maimonides, failure to believe in a single one of these principles places one outside the pale of Judaism.<FL>
<M t2>1) <i>the existence of God</i>
<M e><AF 6>Exalted is the living God, and praised
<M h> <M newbold> יִגְדַּל <M reg> אֱלֹהִים חַי וְיִשְׁתַּבַּח, <FL>
<M e>He exists, and His existence transcends time.
<M h> נִמְצָא וְאֵין עֵת אֶל מְצִיאוּתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>2) <i>God is One</i>
<M e><AF 6>He is One, and there is no unity like His,
<M h> אֶחָד וְאֵין יָחִיד כְּיִחוּדוֹ, <FL>
<M e>He is invisible, His unity is infinitive.
<M h> נֶעְלָם וְגַם אֵין סוֹף לְאַחְדּוּתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>3) <i>God is uncorporeal</i>
<M e><AF 6>He is unlike the corporeal
<M h> אֵין לוֹ דְמוּת הַגּוּף <FL>
<M e>or even the non-corporeal,<M tnt>
<M h> וְאֵינוֹ גוּף, <FL>
<M e>His holiness is beyond comparison.
<M h> לֹא נַעֲרֹךְ אֵלָיו קְדֻשָּׁתוֹ: <FL>
<xx><M tex><M t2>4) <i>God is Eternal</i>
<M e><AF 6>He preceded every being that was created,
<M h> קַדְמוֹן לְכָל דָּבָר אֲשֶׁר נִבְרָא, <FL>
<M e>He was First,
<M h> רִאשׁוֹן <FL>
<M e>and there was no genesis to His beginning.
<M h> וְאֵין רֵאשִׁית לְרֵאשִׁיתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>5) <i>God alone must be worshipped</i>
<M e><AF 6>He is Master of the Universe to every creature,
<M h> הִנּוֹ אֲדוֹן עוֹלָם לְכָל נוֹצָר, <FL>
<M e>(all) proclaim His greatness and His majesty.
<M h> יוֹרֶה גְדֻלָּתוֹ וּמַלְ֒כוּתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>6) <i>Truth of Divine Prophecy</i>
<M t2>The fullness of His prophecy, He bestowed
<M h> שֶֽׁפַע נְבוּאָתוֹ נְתָנוֹ, <FL>
<M e>on those He treasured,
<M h> אֶל אַנְ֒שֵׁי סְגֻלָּתוֹ <FL>
<M e>and in whom He gloried.
<M h> וְתִפְאַרְתּוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>7) <i>Moses was the greatest of all prophets</i>
<M e><AF 6>There never arose in Israel
<M h> לֹא קָם בְּיִשְׂרָאֵל <FL>
<M e>another like Moses,
<M h> כְּמשֶׁה עוֹד, <FL>
<M e>a prophet who beheld God’s image.
<M h> נָבִיא וּמַבִּיט אֶת תְּמוּנָתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>8) <i>Divine revelation of the Torah</i>
<M e><AF 6>The Torah of truth
<M h> תּוֹרַת אֱמֶת <FL>
<M e>the Almighty gave to His people
<M h> נָתַן לְעַמּוֹ אֵל, <FL>
<M e>through His prophet,
<M h> עַל יַד נְבִיאוֹ <FL>
<M e>the trusted one of His house.
<M h> נֶאֱמַן בֵּיתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>9) <i>The Torah is immutable</i>
<M e><AF 6>The Almighty will not exchange
<M h> לֹא יַחֲלִיף הָאֵל <FL>
<M e>nor alter His Law.
<M h> וְלֹא יָמִיר דָּתוֹ, <FL>
<M e>Never will He offer any alternative.
<M h> לְעוֹלָמִים לְזוּלָתוֹ: <FL>
<M tex><M t2>10) <i>God knows the acts and thoughts of man</i>
<M e><AF 6>He scrutinizes and knows our secrets.
<M h> צוֹפֶה וְיוֹדֵֽעַ סְתָרֵֽינוּ, <FL>
<M e>He beholds the end of a thing at its beginning.
<M h> מַבִּיט לְסוֹף דָּבָר בְּקַדְמָתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>11) <i>Divine reward and punishment</i>
<M e><AF 6>He rewards man with kindness
<M h> גּוֹמֵל לְאִישׁ חֶֽסֶד <FL>
<M e>according to his deeds.
<M h> כְּמִפְעָלוֹ, <FL>
<M e>He sends evil to the wicked
<M h> נוֹתֵן לְרָשָׁע רָע <FL>
<M e>according to his wickedness.<M tnt>
<M h> כְּרִשְׁעָתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>12) <i>Belief in the coming of the Messiah</i>
<M e><AF 6>He will send our Messiah at the end of days,
<M h> יִשְׁלַח לְקֵץ הַיָּמִין מְשִׁיחֵֽנוּ, <FL>
<M e>to redeem all who await His final deliverance.
<M h> לִפְדּוֹת מְחַכֵּי קֵץ יְשׁוּעָתוֹ: <FL>
<M t2>13) <i>Divine resurrection of the dead</i>
<M e><AF 6>The Almighty will revive the dead
<M h> מֵתִים יְחַיֶּה אֵל <FL>
<M e>because of His abundant kindness:
<M h> בְּרֹב חַסְדּוֹ, <FL>
<M e>Blessed forever is His praised Name.
<M h> בָּרוּךְ עֲדֵי עַד שֵׁם תְּהִלָּתוֹ: <FL>

<M e>and slumber from my eyelids.

<M e>and hold fast to Your commandments.
<M h> וְדַבְּ֒קֵֽנוּ בְּמִצְוֹתֶֽיךָ, <FL>
<M e>Do not bring us
<M h> וְאַל תְּבִיאֵֽנוּ <FL>

<M e>Do not cause us to be tested,<M tnt>
<M h> וְלֹא לִידֵי נִסָּיוֹן <FL>
<M e>or brought to disgrace.<M tnt>
<M h> וְלֹא לִידֵי בִזָּיוֹן <FL>
<M e>Let us not be ruled over
<M h> וְאַל יִשְׁלֹט בָּֽנוּ <FL>
<M e>by the Evil Inclination.

<M h> וּמֵחָבֵר רָע <FL>

<M e>and to good deeds,

<M h> מֵעַזֵּי פָנִים וּמֵעַזּוּת פָּנִים <FL>
<M e>from an evil man, from an evil companion,

<M h> וּמִשָּׁכֵן רָע <FL>
<M e>from an evil mishap
<M h> וּמִפֶּֽגַע רָע <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>from an evil eye,
<M h> מֵעַֽיִן הָרָע, <FL>
<M e>from a malicious tongue, from slander,

<@02>Akeidah (The Binding of Isaac)
<@02>עקידה
<M t1>Our God and God of our fathers,
<M h> <M newbold> אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ <M reg> וֵאלֹהֵי אֲבוֹתֵֽינוּ <FL>
<M e>remember us favorably before You
<M h> זָכְ֒רֵֽנוּ בְּזִכָּרוֹן טוֹב לְפָנֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>and be mindful of us for
<M h> וּפָקְ֒דֵֽנוּ בִּפְ֒קֻדַּת <FL>
<M e>deliverance and compassion
<M h> יְשׁוּעָה וְרַחֲמִים <FL>
<M e>from the eternal high heavens.
<M h> מִשְּׁ֒מֵי שְׁמֵי קֶֽדֶם <FL>
<M e>Remember in our behalf, Adonoy, our God:
<M h> וּזְ֒כָר לָֽנוּ יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ <FL>
<M e>the love of our ancestors,
<M h> אַהֲבַת הַקַּדְמוֹנִים <FL>
<M e>Abraham, Isaac, and Israel, Your servants;
<M h> אַבְרָהָם יִצְחָק וְיִשְׂרָאֵל עֲבָדֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>the covenant, the kindness,
<M h> אֶת הַבְּ֒רִית וְאֶת הַחֶֽסֶד <FL>
<M e>and the oath which You swore
<M h> וְאֶת הַשְּׁ֒בוּעָה שֶׁנִּשְׁבַּֽעְתָּ <FL>
<M e>to our father Abraham on Mount Moriah,
<M h> לְאַבְרָהָם אָבִֽינוּ בְּהַר הַמֹּרִיָּה <FL>
<M e>and the binding
<M h> וְאֶת הָעֲקֵדָה <FL>
<M e>of Isaac, his son
<M h> שֶׁעָקַד אֶת יִצְחָק בְּנוֹ <FL>
<M tex><M e>on the altar,
<M h> עַל גַּבֵּי הַמִּזְבֵּֽחַ <FL>
<M e>as it is written in Your Torah.<M tnt>
<M h> כַּכָּתוּב בְּתוֹרָתֶֽךָ: <FL>
<M t1>After these events,<M tnt>
<M h> <M newbold> וַיְ֒הִי <M reg> אַחַר הַדְּ֒בָרִים הָאֵֽלֶּה <FL>
<M e>God tested Abraham
<M h> וְהָאֱלֹהִים נִסָּה אֶת-אַבְרָהָם <FL>
<M e>and said to him, "Abraham!"
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר אֵלָיו אַבְרָהָם <FL>
<M e>and he [Abraham] said, "Here I am."
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר הִנֵּֽנִי: <FL>
<M e>He said, "Please, take your son,
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר קַח-נָא אֶת-בִּנְ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>your only one,<M tnt>
<M h> אֶת-יְחִידְ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>whom you love---Isaac---
<M h> אֲשֶׁר-אָהַֽבְתָּ אֶת-יִצְחָק <FL>
<M e>and go to the land of Moriah,
<M h> וְלֶךְ-לְךָ אֶל-אֶֽרֶץ הַמֹּרִיָּה <FL>
<M e>and bring him up as a burnt-offering
<M h> וְהַעֲלֵֽהוּ שָׁם לְעֹלָה <FL>
<M e>on one of the mountains
<M h> עַל אַחַד הֶהָרִים <FL>
<M e>which I will designate to you.
<M h> אֲשֶׁר אֹמַר אֵלֶֽיךָ: <FL>
<M e>Abraham awoke early in the morning,
<M h> וַיַּשְׁכֵּם אַבְרָהָם בַּבֹּֽקֶר <FL>
<M e>saddled his donkey,
<M h> וַיַּחֲבשׁ אֶת-חֲמֹרוֹ <FL>
<M e>and took his two attendants<M tnt> with him,
<M h> וַיִּקַּח אֶת-שְׁנֵי נְעָרָיו אִתּוֹ <FL>
<M e>and also his son Isaac.
<M h> וְאֵת יִצְחָק בְּנוֹ <FL>

<M h> וַיְ֒בַקַּע עֲצֵי עֹלָה <FL>
<M e>and rose up, and went to the place
<M h> וַיָּֽקָם וַיֵּֽלֶךְ אֶל-הַמָּקוֹם <FL>
<M e>that God had designated to him.
<M h> אֲשֶׁר-אָֽמַר-לוֹ הָאֱלֹהִֽים: <FL>
<M e>On the third day,
<M h> בַּיּוֹם הַשְּׁ֒לִישִׁי <FL>

<M h> וַיִּשָּׂא אַבְרָהָם אֶת-עֵינָיו <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>and saw the place from afar.
<M h> וַיַּרְא אֶת-הַמָּקוֹם מֵרָחֹק: <FL>
<M e>Abraham said to his attendants,
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר אַבְרָהָם אֶל-נְעָרָיו <FL>

<M h> שְׁבוּ-לָכֶם פֹּה עִם-הַחֲמוֹר <FL>

<M e>and placed it on his son Isaac.

<M e>Isaac spoke to Abraham his father
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר יִצְחָק אֶל-אַבְרָהָם אָבִיו <FL>
<M e>and said, "Father,"
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר אָבִי <FL>

<M e>And the two of them went together.<M tnt>
<M h> וַיֵּלְ֒כוּ שְׁנֵיהֶם יַחְדָּו: <FL>

<M h> וַיַּעֲרֹךְ אֶת-הָעֵצִים <FL>

<M h> וַיַּעֲקֹד אֶת-יִצְחָק בְּנוֹ <FL>

<M h> וַיָּֽשֶׂם אֹתוֹ עַל-הַמִּזְבֵּֽחַ <FL>
<M e>on top of the wood.
<M h> מִמַּֽעַל לָעֵצִים: <FL>
<M e>Abraham reached out his hand
<M h> וַיִּשְׁלַח אַבְרָהָם אֶת-יָדוֹ <FL>
<M e>and took the knife

<M h> וַיִּקְרָא אֵלָיו מַלְאַךְ יְהֹוָה <FL>

<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר אַבְרָהָם אַבְרָהָם <FL>
<M e>and he said, "Here I am."
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר הִנֵּֽנִי: <FL>
<M e>He [God] said,
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר <FL>
<M e>"Do not harm the boy,
<M h> אַל-תִּשְׁלַח יָֽדְ֒ךָ אֶל-הַנַּֽעַר <FL>
<M e>nor do anything to him;
<M h> וְאַל-תַּֽעַשׂ לוֹ מְאוּמָה <FL>
<M e>for now I know
<M h> כִּי עַתָּה יָדַֽעְתִּי <FL>
<M e>that you are one who fears God

<@02>בקשות
<M t1>A person should always be in fear of God,
<M h> <M newbold> לְעוֹלָם <M reg> יְהֵא אָדָם יְרֵא שָׁמַֽיִם <FL>
<M e>privately as well as openly,<M tnt>
<M h> בַּסֵּֽתֶר וּבַגָּלוּי <FL>
<M e>[he should] admit the truth,<M tnt>
<M h> וּמוֹדֶה עַל הָאֱמֶת <FL>
<M e>and speak truth in his heart,<M tnt>
<M h> וְדוֹבֵר אֱמֶת בִּלְ֒בָבוֹ <FL>
<M e>and rise early and proclaim:
<M h> וְיַשְׁכֵּם וְיֹאמַר: <FL>
<M t1>Lord of all the worlds
<M h> רִבּוֹן כָּל הָעוֹלָמִים <FL>
<M e>and Master of masters!
<M h> וַאֲדוֹנֵי הָאֲדוֹנִים,
<M e>Not on account of our righteousness
<M h> לֹא עַל צִדְ֒קוֹתֵֽינוּ <FL>
<M e>do we offer our supplications before You,
<M h> אֲנַֽחְנוּ מַפִּילִים תַּחֲנוּנֵֽינוּ לְפָנֶֽיךָ <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>but on account of Your abundant mercy.
<M h> כִּי עַל רַחֲמֶֽיךָ הָרַבִּים, <FL>
<M e>What are we? What is our life?

<M e>What are our acts of kindness?
<M h> מֶה חַסְדֵּֽנוּ, <FL>
<M e>What is our righteousness?
<M h> מַה צִּדְ֒קוֹתֵֽינוּ, <FL>
<M e>What is our deliverance?<M tnt>
<M h> מַה יְּשׁוּעָתֵֽנוּ,
<M e>What is our strength? What is our might?
<M h> מַה כֹּחֵֽנוּ מַה גְּבוּרָתֵֽנוּ, <FL>
<M e>What can we say before You,

<M h> לְעֵינֵיכֶם אָמַר יְהֹוָה: <FL>
<@02>Korbanos (Sacrificial Offerings)
<@02>קרבנות
<M ex><EM><EN>The Talmud (<i>Maseches Menachos</i> 110a) states: Rabbi Isaac asked, "Why does it say (<i>Leviticus</i> 6:18; 7:1) This is the <i>law</i> of the sin-offering, this is the <i>law</i> of the guilt-offering? To teach us that when one <i>studies</i> the <i>law</i> of the sin-offering, it is considered as though he had actually brought it on the Altar, and when one <i>studies</i> the <i>law</i> of the guilt-offering, it is as though he actually brought it on the Altar."<FL>
<EM><EN>Rather than merely recite the following portions, study them and attempt to learn about the laws and significance of the various sacrifices.<FL>
<M in>Exodus</i> 30:17-21<FC>
<M t2>And Adonoy spoke to Moses to say:
<M h> <M newbold> וַיְדַבֵּר <M reg> יְהֹוָה אֶל-משֶׁה לֵּאמֹר: <FL>
<M e>Make a copper laver
<M h> וְעָשִֽׂיתָ כִּיּוֹר נְחֽשֶׁת <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>and a copper base, for washing;
<M h> וְכַנּוֹ נְחֽשֶׁת לְרָחְצָה <FL>
<M e>and place it
<M h> וְנָתַתָּ אֹת֒וֹ <FL>
<M e>between the Tent of Meeting and the Altar,
<M h> בֵּין-אֹֽהֶל מוֹעֵד וּבֵין הַמִּזְבֵּֽחַ <FL>
<M e>and put water in it.
<M h> וְנָתַתָּ שָֽׁמָּה מָֽיִם: <FL>
<M e>Aaron and his sons will wash from it,
<M h> וְרָחֲצוּ אַהֲרֹן וּבָנָיו מִמֶּֽנּוּ <FL>
<M e>their hands and their feet.<M tnt>
<M h> אֶת-יְדֵיהֶם וְאֶת-רַגְלֵיהֶם: <FL>
<M e>Upon entering the Tent of Meeting
<M h> בְּבֹאָם אֶל-אֹֽהֶל מוֹעֵד <FL>
<M e>they will wash with water that they not die,
<M h> יִרְחֲצוּ-מַֽיִם וְלֹא יָמֻֽתוּ <FL>
<M e>or whenever they approach the Altar

<M e>to serve, to burn a fire-offering to Adonoy.

<M e>that they not die;
<M h> וְלֹא יָמֻֽתוּ <FL>

<@02>Korban Tamid (Daily Offering)
<@02>קרבן תמיד
<M ex><EM><EN>The <i>Tamid</i>-offerings, two daily offerings of one lamb at a time, were offered once in the morning and once in the afternoon. The former was the first public-offering brought on the Altar each day. And the latter terminated the day’s offerings. These animals were purchased from the annual half-shekel gifts of the people and were offered on behalf of the entire Jewish People. Before reading this passage we offer a brief prayer.<FL>
<M in>Some do not say the following prayer on Sabbath and Yom Tov.<FC>
<M t2>May it be Your will,
<M h> <M newbold> יְהִי רָצוֹן <M reg> מִלְּ֒פָנֶֽיךָ, <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, our God and God of our fathers,

<M e>to have compassion on us,

<M h>

<M t2>The Rabbis taught:
<M h> <M newbold> תָּנוּ רַבָּנָן <M reg> <FL>
<M e>How was the incense compounded?
<M h> פִּטּוּם הַקְּ֒טֹֽרֶת כֵּיצַד <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>Three hundred and sixty-eight
<M h> שְׁלֹש מֵאוֹת וְשִׁשִּׁים וּשְׁ֒מוֹנָה <FL>
<M e><i>manim</i><M tnt> were comprised therein,
<M h> מָנִים הָיוּ בָהּ, <FL>
<M e>three hundred and sixty-five
<M h> שְׁלֹש מֵאוֹת וְשִׁשִּׁים וַחֲמִשָּׁה <FL>
<M e>corresponding to
<M h> כְּמִנְיַן <FL>
<M e>the number of days in the solar year,
<M h> יְמוֹת הַחַמָּה <FL>
<M e>one <i>maneh</i> for each day---
<M h> מָנֶה לְכָל יוֹם, <FL>
<M e>half in the morning
<M h> פְּרַס בַּשַּׁחֲרִית <FL>
<M e>and half in the afternoon.
<M h> וּפְ֒רַס בֵּין הָעַרְבָּֽיִם, <FL>
<M e>From the three remaining <i>manim</i>
<M h> וּשְׁ֒לשָׁה מָנִים יְתֵרִים <FL>
<M e>the Kohein Gadol brought
<M h> שֶׁמֵּהֶם מַכְנִיס כֹּהֵן גָּדוֹל <FL>
<M e>two handfuls [into the Holy of Holies]
<M h> מְלֹא חָפְנָיו <FL>
<M e>on Yom Kippur;
<M h> בְּיוֹם הַכִּפּוּרִים, <FL>
<M e>[for which purpose] they were put back
<M h> וּמַחֲזִירָן <FL>
<M e>into the mortar
<M h> לְמַכְתֶּֽשֶׁת <FL>
<M e>on the eve of Yom Kippur,
<M h> בְּעֶֽרֶב יוֹם הַכִּפּוּרִים, <FL>
<M e>and ground [again] very thoroughly,
<M h> וְשׁוֹחֲקָן יָפֶה יָפֶה <FL>
<M e>in order to make them very fine.
<M h> כְּדֵי שֶׁתְּ֒הֵא דַקָּה מִן הַדַּקָּה, <FL>
<M e>Eleven kinds of spices were used for it.
<M h> וְאַחַד עָשָׂר סַמָּנִים הָֽיוּ בָהּ, <FL>
<M e>They were:
<M h> וְאֵֽלּוּ הֵן <FL>
<M e>1) balm, 2) onycha,
<M h> הַצֳּרִי וְהַצִּפֹּֽרֶן <FL>
<M e>3) galbanum, 4) frankincense---
<M h> הַחֶלְבְּנָה וְהַלְּ֒בוֹנָה <FL>
<M e>by weight, seventy <i>maneh</i> of each;
<M h> מִשְׁקַל שִׁבְעִים שִׁבְעִים מָנֶה, <FL>
<M e>5) myrrh, 6) cassia,
<M h> מוֹר וּקְ֒צִיעָה <FL>
<M e>7) spikenard and 8) saffron---
<M h> שִׁבֹּֽלֶת נֵרְדְּ וְכַרְכֹּם <FL>
<M e>in weight
<M h> מִשְׁקַל <FL>
<M e>sixteen <i>maneh</i> of each;
<M h> שִׁשָּׁה עָשָׂר שִׁשָּׁה עָשָׂר מָנֶה, <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>9) twelve <i>maneh</i> of costus,
<M h> הַקּשְׁטְ שְׁנֵים עָשָׂר <FL>
<M e>10) three of aromatic bark,
<M h> וְקִלּוּפָה שְׁלשָׁה <FL>
<M e>and 11) nine of cinnamon.
<M h> וְקִנָּמוֹן תִּשְׁעָה, <FL>
<M e>[Also used in the incense compound were:]
<M h><FL>
<M e>Nine <i>kabin</i><M tnt> of Carshina lye,
<M h> בֹּרִית כַּרְשִׁינָה תִּשְׁעָה קַבִּין, <FL>
<M e>Cyprus wine [measuring]
<M h> יֵין קַפְרִיסִין <FL>
<M e>three <i>s’in</i> and three <i>kabin</i>---
<M h> סְאִין תְּלָתָא וְקַבִּין תְּלָתָא, <FL>
<M e>if he had no Cyprus wine,
<M h> וְאִם אֵין לוֹ יֵין קַפְרִיסִין <FL>
<M e>he could use strong white wine---
<M h> מֵבִיא חֲמַר חִוּרְיָן עַתִּיק, <FL>
<M e>a fourth of a <i>kab</i> of Sodom salt,
<M h> מֶֽלַח סְדוֹמִית רֹֽבַע הַקָּב, <FL>
<M e>and a minute quantity of <i>maaleh ashan.</i><M tnt>
<M h> מַעֲלֶה עָשָׁן כָּל שֶׁהוּא, <FL>
<M e>Rabbi Nosson of Babylonia says,
<M h> רַבִּי נָתָן הַבַּבְלִי אוֹמֵר <FL>
<M e>"Jordan amber was added
<M h> אַף כִּפַּת הַיַּרְדֵּן
<M e>of a minute quantity,
<M h> כָּל שֶׁהוּא, <FL>
<M e>and if one added honey,<M tnt>
<M h> וְאִם נָֽתַן בָּהּ דְּבַשׁ
<M e>it (the incense) became unfit;
<M h> פְּסָלָהּ <FL>
<M e>and if one omitted<M tnt> any of its spices
<M h> וְאִם חִסַּר אַחַת מִכָּל סַמָּנֶֽיהָ <FL>
<M e>he was liable to the death penalty."<M tnt>
<M h> חַיָּב מִיתָה: <FL>
<M t1>Rabbi Shimon ben Gamliel says:
<M h> <M newbold> רַבָּן שִׁמְעוֹן בֶּן גַּמְלִיאֵל <M reg> אוֹמֵר <FL>
<M e>"The balm is nothing but sap
<M h> הַצֳּרִי אֵינוֹ אֶלָּא שְׂרָף <FL>
<M e>which drips from the balsam tree.
<M h> הַנּוֹטֵף מֵעֲצֵי הַקְּ֒טָף, <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>the lye of Carshina was used
<M h> בֹּרִית כַּרְשִׁינָה <FL>
<M e>for rubbing the onycha
<M h> שֶׁשָׁפִין בָּה אֶת הַצִפֹּרֶן <FL>
<M e>in order to refine its appearance.
<M h> כִּדֵי שֶׁתְּ֒הֵא נָאֶה <FL>
<M e>The Cyprus wine was used
<M h> יֵין קַפְרִיסִין <FL>
<M e>to soak the onycha
<M h> שֶׁשׁוֹרִין בּוֹ אֶת הַצִפֹּרֶן <FL>
<M e>to give it a pungent odor.
<M h> כְּדֵי שֶׁתְּ֒הֵא עַזָּה, <FL>
<M e>Though the water of Raglayim<M tnt>
<M h> וַהֲלֹא מֵי רַגְלַֽיִם <FL>
<M e>was well suited for that purpose,
<M h> יָפִין לָהּ <FL>
<M e>they did not bring
<M h> אֶלָּא שֶׁאֵין מַכְנִיסִין <FL>
<M e>the water of Raglayim into the Temple
<M h> מֵי רַגְלַֽיִם בַּמִּקְדָּשׁ <FL>
<M e>because it would be disrespectful.<M tnt>
<M h> מִפְּנֵי הַכָּבוֹד: <FL>
<M t1>It was taught in a <i>Boraysa</i>:
<M h> <M newbold> תַּנְיָא <M reg> <FL>
<M e>Rabbi Nosson says,
<M h> רַבִּי נָתָן אוֹמֵר <FL>
<M e>"While [the Kohein] ground [the incense]
<M h> כְּשֶׁהוּא שׁוֹחֵק <FL>
<M e>he would say,
<M h> אוֹמֵר <FL>
<M e><i>‘Hodeik heiteiv, heiteiv hodeik,’</i>
<M h> הָדֵק הֵיטֵב הֵיטֵב הָדֵק <FL>
<M e>because the sound<M tnt> is good for the spices.
<M h> מִפְּ֒נֵי שֶׁהַקּוֹל יָפֶה לַבְּ֒שָׂמִים, <FL>
<M e>If half<M tnt> the quantity of incense was prepared
<M h> פִּטְּ֒מָהּ לַחֲצָאִין <FL>
<M e>it was acceptable,
<M h> כְּשֵׁרָה <FL>
<M e>but if only a third
<M h> לִשְׁ֒לִישׁ
<M e>or a fourth [of it was prepared]
<M h> וְלִרְ֒בִֽיעַ <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>we have not heard<M tnt>
<M h> לֹא שָׁמַֽעְנוּ: <FL>
<M e>[whether it was acceptable."]
<M h>
<M e>Rabbi Yehuda said,
<M h> אָמַר רַבִּי יְהוּדָה <FL>
<M e>"This is the general rule:
<M h> זֶה הַכְּ֒לָל <FL>
<M e>If [it was prepared with all its ingredients]
<M h> אִם <FL>
<M e>in the correct proportion,
<M h> כְּמִדָּתָהּ <FL>
<M e>it is acceptable
<M h> כְּשֵׁרָה <FL>
<M e>even if only half was prepared;
<M h> לַחֲצָאִין <FL>
<M e>but if he left out any of its spices,
<M h> וְאִם חִסַּר אַחַת מִכָּל סַמָּנֶֽיהָ <FL>
<M e>he was liable for the death penalty.
<M h> חַיָּב מִיתָה: <FL>
<M t1>It was taught in a <i>Boraysa</i>:
<M h> <M newbold> תַּנְיָא <M reg> <FL>
<M e>Bar Kappara says,
<M h> בַּר קַפָּרָא אוֹמֵר <FL>
<M e>"Once in sixty or seventy years<M tnt>
<M h> אַחַת לְשִׁשִּׁים אוֹ לְשִׁבְעִים שָׁנָה <FL>
<M e>the accumulated surplus was sufficient
<M h> הָיְ֒תָה בָאָה שֶׁל שִׁירַֽיִם <FL>
<M e>to provide half
<M h> לַחֲצָאִין: <FL>
<M e>[the yearly quantity of incense."]
<M h>
<M e>Bar Kappara also taught,
<M h> וְעוֹד תָּנֵי בַּר קַפָּרָא <FL>
<M e>"If he would have put into it
<M h> אִלּוּ הָיָה נוֹתֵן בָּהּ <FL>
<M e>a minute quantity of honey,
<M h> קוֹרְ֒טוֹב שֶׁל דְּבַשׁ <FL>
<M e>no one could have withstood [resisted]
<M h> אֵין אָדָם יָכוֹל לַעֲמֹד <FL>
<M e>the scent.
<M h> מִפְּ֒נֵי רֵיחָהּ <FL>
<M e>Why was no honey mixed with it?
<M h> וְלָֽמָּה אֵין מְעָרְ֒בִין בָּהּ דְּבַשׁ <FL>
<M e>Because the Torah says, (<i>Leviticus</i> 2:11)
<M h> מִפְּ֒נֵי שֶׁהַתּוֹרָה אָמְ֒רָה <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>For any leaven or honey,
<M h> כִּי כָל-שְׂאֹר וְכָל-דְּבַשׁ <FL>
<M e>do not burn from them,
<M h> לֹא-תַקְטִֽירוּ מִמֶּֽנּוּ <FL>
<M e>[as] a fire-offering to Adonoy."
<M h> אִשֶּׁה לַיהוָֹה: <FL>
<M in>Recite each of these verses three times:<FC>
<M t2>Adonoy of Hosts is with us,
<M h> יְהֹוָה צְבָאוֹת עִמָּֽנוּ <FL>
<M e>a stronghold for us is the God of Jacob, Selah!
<M h> מִשְׂגַּב-לָֽנוּ אֱלֹהֵי יַעֲקֹב סֶֽלָה: <FL>
<M e>Adonoy of Hosts,
<M h> יְהֹוָה צְבָאוֹת <FL>
<M e>fortunate is the man who trusts in You.
<M h> אַשְׁרֵי אָדָם בֹּטֵֽחַ בָּךְ: <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, deliver [us]!
<M h> יְהֹוָה הוֹשִֽׁיעָה <FL>
<M e>The King will answer us on the day we call.
<M h> הַמֶּֽלֶךְ יַעֲנֵֽנוּ בְיוֹם-קָרְ֒אֵֽנוּ: <FL>
<M t1>You are my shelter;
<M h> אַתָּה סֵֽתֶר לִי <FL>
<M e>from distress You preserve me;

<M h> רָנֵּי פַלֵּט תְּסוֹבְ֒בֵֽנִי
<M e>Selah!
<M h> סֶֽלָה: <FL>

<M h> וְעָרְ֒בָה לַיהוָֹה <FL>
<M e>with the offerings of Judah and Jerusalem,
<M h> מִנְחַת יְהוּדָה וִירוּשָׁלָֽםִ <FL>
<M e>as in the days of old and in earlier years.
<M h> כִּימֵי עוֹלָם וּכְ֒שָׁנִים קַדְמֹנִיּוֹת: <FL>
<M t1>Abbaye listed

<M h> וְאַלִּבָּא דְאַבָּא שָׁאוּל, <FL>
<M e>the [arranging on the Altar

<M h> קוֹדֶֽמֶת <FL>

<M h>

<M h> הָעֹלָה <FL>

<M t2>Please, by the force of Your great right hand,

<M e>release the bound one.

<M ex>The following sequence of Mishnayos and the selection from <i>Sifra</i> "Rabbi Yishmael Says," were inserted after the Scriptural selections dealing with daily-offerings in order to give every Jew the opportunity to study/recite daily, the minimum of selections from Scripture, Mishnah, and Talmud. Even though <i>Sifra</i> is not actually a Talmudic tractate, it is a Tanaitic expansion of Mishnah. (See <i>Shulchan Aruch, Orach<i> Chaim</i> 50:1).<FL>
<M ex>The following are <i>Mishnayos</i> found in the fifth chapter of <i>Maseches Zevachim.</i><FL>

<M h><FL>

<M t1>Rabbi Yishmael says:
<M h> <M newbold> רַבִּי יִשְׁמָעֵאל <M reg> אוֹמֵר <FL>
<M e>through thirteen methods
<M h> בִּשְׁ֒לשׁ עֶשְׂרֵה מִדּוֹת <FL>
<M e>the Torah is expounded:
<M h> הַתּוֹרָה נִדְרֶֽשֶׁת בָּהֵן: <FL>
<M t2>1) A conclusion drawn from a minor
<M h> מִקַּל וָחֹֽמֶר, <FL>
<M e>or lenient law,
<M h><FL>
<M e>to a major or more strict one.
<M h><FL>
<M t2>2) A clarification based on identical words
<M h> וּמִגְּ֒זֵרָה שָׁוָה, <FL>
<M e>or terms in the Biblical text.
<M h><FL>
<M t2>3) A principle derived from one Biblical text
<M h> מִבִּנְיַן אָב מִכָּתוּב אֶחָד, <FL>
<M e>or from two Biblical texts.
<M h> וּמִבִּנְיַן אָב מִשְּׁ֒נֵי כְתוּבִים, <FL>
<M t2>4) A rule followed by a detail.
<M h> מִכְּ֒לָל וּפְ֒רָט, <FL>
<M t2>5) A detail followed by a rule.
<M h> וּמִפְּ֒רָט וּכְ֒לָל, <FL>
<M t2>6) A rule followed by a detail,
<M h> כְּלָל וּפְ֒רָט <FL>
<M e>which is in turn followed by a rule,
<M h> וּכְ֒לָל <FL>
<M e>may infer only what is similar to the detail.
<M h> אִי אַתָּה דָן אֶלָּא כְּעֵין הַפְּ֒רָט, <FL>
<M t2>7) When a general rule requires an explicit rule;
<M h> מִכְּ֒לָל שֶׁהוּא צָרִיךְ לִפְ֒רָט <FL>
<M e>when an explicit rule requires generalization.
<M h> וּמִפְּ֒רָט שֶׁהוּא צָרִיךְ לִכְ֒לָל, <FL>
<M t2>8) Something included in a general rule,
<M h> כָּל דָּבָר שֶׁהָיָה בִּכְ֒לָל <FL>
<M e>which was singled out to teach---
<M h> וְיָצָא מִן הַכְּ֒לָל לְלַמֵּד <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>was not singled out to teach about itself,
<M h> לֹא לְלַמֵּד עַל עַצְמוֹ יָצָא <FL>
<M e>but to teach (something new)
<M h> אֶלָּא לְלַמֵּד <FL>
<M e>concerning the rule as a whole.
<M h> עַל הַכְּ֒לָל כֻּלּוֹ יָצָא, <FL>
<M t2>9) Something that was included in a rule
<M h> כָּל דָּבָר שֶׁהָיָה בִּכְ֒לָל <FL>
<M e>and was singled out in a case
<M h> וְיָצָא לִטְעֹן טֹֽעַן אֶחָד <FL>
<M e>similar to its rule,
<M h> שֶׁהוּא כְעִנְיָנוֹ <FL>
<M e>---it was singled out to lessen
<M h> יָצָא לְהָקֵל <FL>
<M e>not to increase the severity of the case.
<M h> וְלֹא לְהַחֲמִיר, <FL>
<M t2>10) Something that was included in a rule
<M h> כָּל דָּבָר שֶׁהָיָה בִּכְלָל <FL>
<M e>and was singled out in a case
<M h> וְיָצָא לִטְעֹן טֹֽעַן אַחֵר <FL>
<M e>which is not similar to its rule,
<M h> שֶׁלֹּא כְעִנְיָנוֹ <FL>
<M e>---it was singled out either to lessen
<M h> יָצָא לְהָקֵל <FL>
<M e>or to increase the severity of the case.
<M h> וּלְ֒הַחֲמִיר, <FL>
<M t2>11) Something that was included in a rule
<M h> כָּל דָּבָר שֶׁהָיָה בִּכְ֒לָל <FL>
<M e>and was singled out for a new stipulation---
<M h> וְיָצָא לִדּוֹן בַּדָּבָר הֶחָדָשׁ <FL>
<M e>does not revert to its rule
<M h> אִי אַתָּה יָכוֹל לְהַחֲזִירוֹ לִכְ֒לָלוֹ <FL>
<M e>unless Scripture restores it to its rule
<M h> עַד שֶׁיַּחֲזִירֶֽנּוּ הַכָּתוּב לִכְ֒לָלוֹ <FL>
<M e>expressly.
<M h> בְּפֵרוּשׁ, <FL>
<M t2>12) A matter deduced from its context,
<M h> דָּבָר הַלָּמֵד מֵעִנְיָנוֹ <FL>
<M e>or from a subsequent expression.
<M h> וְדָבָר הַלָּמֵד מִסּוֹפוֹ, <FL>
<M t2>13) Also, two passages that
<M h> וְכֵן שְׁנֵי כְתוּבִים <FL>
<M e>contradict each other
<M h> הַמַּכְחִישִׁים זֶה אֶת זֶה <FL>
<M e>until a third passage
<M h> עַד שֶׁיָּבֹא הַכָּתוּב הַשְּׁ֒לִישִׁי <FL>
<M e>reconciles them.
<M h> וְיַכְרִֽיעַ בֵּינֵיהֶם: <FL>
<M t1>May it be Your will
<M h> <M chaz> יְהִי רָצוֹן מִלְּ֒פָנֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, our God and God of our fathers,
<M h> יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ וֵאלֹהֵי אֲבוֹתֵֽינוּ <FL>
<M e>that the Holy Temple be rebuilt
<M h> שֶׁיִּבָּנֶה בֵּית הַמִּקְדָּשׁ <FL>
<M e>speedily in our days:
<M h> בִּמְ֒הֵרָה בְיָמֵֽינוּ <FL>
<M tex><M e>and grant us our share in Your Torah.
<M h> וְתֵן חֶלְקֵֽנוּ בְּתוֹרָתֶֽךָ: <FL>
<M e>And there we will serve You reverently
<M h> וְשָׁם נַעֲבָדְ֒ךָ בְּיִרְאָה <FL>
<M e>as in the days of old,
<M h> כִּימֵי עוֹלָם <FL>
<M e>and in earlier years.
<M h> וּכְ֒שָׁנִים קַדְמוֹנִיּוֹת: <FL>
<@02>Kaddish d’Rabanan
<@02>קדיש דרבנן
<M ex><EM><EN>Kaddish is not the name generally given to this prayer in the Talmud. It is referred to there as "May His great Name<NS>.<NS>.<NS>.", because the congregational response beginning with these words is the heart of this prayer. Only in one minor tractate, (<i>Maseches Soferim</i> 16, 19, and 21) is it referred to as Kaddish.<FL>
<EM><EN>Composed primarily in Aramaic, the language spoken and understood by most Jews in the Second Temple period (See <i>Tosafos</i> to <i>Maseches Berachos</i> 3a), nevertheless, several Hebrew phrases, which were familiar even to the unschooled, were also incorporated in the prayer.<FL>
<EM><EN>This particular form of Kaddish d’Rabanan, is so named because of the insertion of the paragraph which begins with the words "Upon Israel and upon our Sages, etc." This Kaddish is recited following the study of Talmud or Midrash and invokes God’s blessings on the Sages of Jewry, the transmitters of the Oral Torah.<FL>
<M t2>Exalted and sanctified<M tnt> be His great Name

<M e>in the world which He created

<@02>Pesukei Dezimrah
<@02>פסוקי דזמרה
<M ex><EM><EN>The following sequence of prayers until Yishtabach (p. 94) is called <i>Pesukei Dezimrah</i> (verses of praise). These selected Scriptural passages were arranged by the Gaonim of the ninth century, in fulfillment of the Talmudic statement (<i>Maseches<i> Berachos</i> 32a), "A person should always praise God first and make his requests [offer his prayers] afterwards." Beginning with the following prayer, it is forbidden to interrupt your prayer with conversation until after the <i>Shemoneh Esrei</i> (p. 118).<FL>
<EM><EN>You are permitted to answer Amein, respond to <i>Barechu, Kaddish</i> and to say <i>Kedushah</i> even though you are in the midst of <i>Pesukei Dezimrah</i>. You are also permitted to say <i>Modim d’Rabbonon</i> and the first verse of the <i>Shema</i> together with the congregation.<FL>
﻿<VER Kivun Ltd. Dagesh Professional/PC, Version 0.98U><MACROFILE G.DGM><M 00><M ex><EM><EN>If you are concerned that the saying of <i>Kerias Shema</i> will not be within the proper time should you follow the regular order of prayers, you are permitted to recite the entire <i>Kerias Shema</i> during the <i>Pesukei Dezimrah</i>.<FL>
<@02>Hodu
<@02>הודו
<M ex><EM><EN>The first 28 verses of this section are taken from <i>1 Chronicles</i> 16:8-36, and the first 15 are almost identical with the first fifteen verses of Psalms 105. These prayers are mentioned in <i>Maseches Soferim.</i><FL>
<M t2>Give thanks to Adonoy, proclaim His Name;
<M h> <M newbold> הוֹדוּ לַיהוָֹה <M reg> קִרְ֒אוּ בִּשְׁ֒מוֹ <FL>

<M h> שִֽׁירוּ לוֹ זַמְּ֒רוּ-לוֹ <FL>

<M h> הִתְהַלְּ֒לוּ בְּשֵׁם קָדְשׁוֹ <FL>

<M h> יִשְׂמַח לֵב <FL>
<M e>of those who seek<M tnt> Adonoy.

<M h> בַּקְּ֒שׁוּ פָנָיו תָּמִיד: <FL>
<M e>Remember the wonders He has performed,
<M h> זִכְ֒רוּ נִפְלְ֒אֹתָיו אֲשֶׁר עָשָׂה <FL>

<M e>Then the trees of the forest will sing with joy,
<M h> אָז יְרַנְּ֒נוּ עֲצֵי הַיָּעַר <FL>
<M e>[receding] before Adonoy
<M h> מִלִּפְ֒נֵי יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>when He comes to judge the earth.
<M h> כִּי-בָא לִשְׁפּוֹט אֶת-הָאָֽרֶץ: <FL>
<M e>Give thanks to Adonoy, for He is good,
<M h> הוֹדוּ לַיהוָֹה כִּי טוֹב <FL>
<M e>for His kindness is everlasting.
<M h> כִּי לְעוֹלָם חַסְדּוֹ: <FL>
<M e>And say, "Deliver us, God of our deliverance;
<M h> וְאִמְ֒רוּ הוֹשִׁיעֵֽנוּ אֱלֹהֵי יִשְׁעֵֽנוּ <FL>
<M e>gather us and save us from the nations,
<M h> וְקַבְּ֒צֵֽנוּ וְהַצִּילֵֽנוּ מִן-הַגּוֹיִם <FL>
<M e>to give thanks to Your holy Name,
<M h> לְהוֹדוֹת לְשֵׁם קָדְשֶֽׁךָ <FL>
<M e>to be extolled in Your praise."<M tnt>
<M h> לְהִשְׁתַּבֵּֽחַ בִּתְ֒הִלָּתֶֽךָ: <FL>
<M e>Blessed is Adonoy, the God of Israel
<M h> בָּרוּךְ יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהֵי יִשְׂרָאֵל <FL>
<M e>for all eternity,
<M h> מִן-הָעוֹלָם וְעַד הָעֹלָם <FL>
<M e>and all the people said: "Amein"
<M h> וַיֹּאמְ֒רוּ כָל-הָעָם אָמֵן <FL>
<M e>and [they] praised Adonoy."
<M h> וְהַלֵּל לַיהוָֹה: <FL>

<@02>Mizmor Shir
<@02>מזמור שיר
<M ex><EM><EN>Psalm 30, once used to inaugurate the Holy Temple, is used today to inaugurate our daily prayers, for the synagogue is a "Holy Temple in miniature" and our prayers take the place of the sacrifices. It is both a prayer for success and a declaration of thanksgiving.<FL>
<M t2>A Psalm,
<M h> <M newbold> מִזְמוֹר <M reg> <FL>
<M e>a song for the inauguration of the Temple,
<M h> שִׁיר-חֲנֻכַּת הַבַּֽיִת <FL>
<M e>by David.<M tnt>
<M h> לְדָוִד: <FL>
<M e>I will exalt You, Adonoy,
<M h> אֲרוֹמִמְ֒ךָ יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>for You have upheld me,<M tnt>
<M h> כִּי דִלִּיתָֽנִי <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>and not let my foes rejoice over me.
<M h> וְלֹא-שִׂמַּֽחְתָּ אֹיְ֒בַי לִי: <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, my God,
<M h> יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהָי <FL>
<M e>I cried out to You, and You healed me.
<M h> שִׁוּעְתִּי אֵלֶֽיךָ וַתִּרְפָּאֵֽנִי: <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, You have raised
<M h> יְהֹוָה הֶעֱלִֽיתָ <FL>
<M e>my soul from the lower world.
<M h> מִן-שְׁאוֹל נַפְשִׁי <FL>
<M e>You have kept me alive,
<M h> חִיִּיתַֽנִי
<M e>lest I descend to the Pit.
<M h> מִיָּרְ֒דִי-בוֹר: <FL>
<M e>Sing to Adonoy, [you,] His pious ones,
<M h> זַמְּ֒רוּ לַיהוָֹה חֲסִידָיו <FL>
<M e>and give thanks to His holy Name.<M tnt>
<M h> וְהוֹדוּ לְזֵֽכֶר קָדְשׁוֹ: <FL>
<M e>For His anger lasts only a moment,<M tnt>
<M h> כִּי רֶֽגַע בְּאַפּוֹ <FL>
<M e>but there is [long] life, in His conciliation.
<M h> חַיִּים בִּרְצוֹנוֹ <FL>
<M e>In the evening, one retires weeping,
<M h> בָּעֶֽרֶב יָלִין בֶּֽכִי <FL>
<M e>but in the morning there is [a cry of] joy!
<M h> וְלַבֹּֽקֶר רִנָּה: <FL>
<M e>I said, in my serenity,
<M h> וַאֲנִי אָמַֽרְתִּי בְשַׁלְוִי <FL>
<M e>I would never be moved.
<M h> בַּל-אֶמּוֹט לְעוֹלָם: <FL>
<M e>[But,] Adonoy, it was Your will [alone]
<M h> יְהֹוָה בִּרְ֒צוֹנְ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>that established my mountain
<M h> הֶעֱמַֽדְתָּה לְהַרְרִי
<M e>as a stronghold.
<M h> עֹז <FL>
<M e>When You concealed Your Presence,
<M h> הִסְתַּֽרְתָּ פָנֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>I was terrified.
<M h> הָיִֽיתִי נִבְהָל: <FL>
<M e>To You, Adonoy, I called,
<M h> אֵלֶֽיךָ יְהֹוָה אֶקְרָא <FL>
<M e>and my Master I beseeched.
<M h> וְאֶל-אֲדֹנָי אֶתְחַנָּן: <FL>
<M e>What gain is there
<M h> מַה-בֶּֽצַע <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>in [the shedding of] my blood?
<M h> בְּדָמִי <FL>
<M e>In my going down to destruction?
<M h> בְּרִדְתִּי אֶל שָֽׁחַת <FL>
<M e>Will the dust acknowledge You?
<M h> הֲיוֹדְ֒ךָ עָפָר <FL>
<M e>Will it proclaim Your truth?
<M h> הֲיַגִּיד אֲמִתֶּֽךָ: <FL>
<M e>Hear [me] Adonoy, and be gracious to me,
<M h> שְׁמַע יְהֹוָה וְחָנֵּֽנִי <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, be a help to me.
<M h> יְהֹוָה הֱיֵה-עֹזֵר לִי: <FL>
<M e>You have turned my mourning into dancing,
<M h> <M chaz> הָפַֽכְתָּ מִסְפְּדִי לְמָחוֹל לִי <FL>
<M e>You have loosened my sackcloth
<M h> פִּתַּחְתָּ שַׂקִּי <FL>
<M e>and supported me with joy.
<M h> וַתְּ֒אַזְּ֒רֵֽנִי שִׂמְחָה: <FL>
<M e>In order that my soul<M tnt> might sing to You
<M h> לְמַֽעַן יְזַמֶּרְ֒ךָ כָבוֹד <FL>
<M e>and not be stilled,
<M h> וְלֹא יִדֹּם <FL>
<M e>Adonoy, my God, forever will I thank You.
<M h> יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהַי לְעוֹלָם אוֹדֶֽךָּ: <FL>
<M t1>Adonoy is King, Adonoy was King
<M h> <M newbold> יְהוָֹה <M reg> מֶֽלֶךְ, יְהוָֹה מָלָֽךְ,
<M e>Adonoy will be King forever and ever.
<M h> יְהוָֹה יִמְלֹךְ, לְעֹלָם וָעֶד:
<M e>Adonoy is King, Adonoy was King
<M h> יְהוָֹה מֶֽלֶךְ, יְהוָֹה מָלָֽךְ,
<M e>Adonoy will be King forever and ever.
<M h> יְהוָֹה יִמְלֹךְ, לְעֹלָם וָעֶד:
<M e>And Adonoy will be King
<M h> וְהָיָה יְהוָֹה לְמֶֽלֶךְ
<M e>over the whole earth;
<M h> עַל-כָּל-הָאָֽרֶץ,
<M e>on that day Adonoy will be One
<M h> בַּיּוֹם הַהוּא יִהְיֶה יְהוָֹה אֶחָד,
<M e>and His Name One.
<M h> וּשְׁ֒מוֹ אֶחָד:
<M e>Deliver us Adonoy, our God,
<M h> הֽוֹשִׁיעֵֽנוּ יְהוָֹה אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ,
<M e>and gather us from among the nations,
<M h> וְקַבְּ֒צֵֽנוּ מִן-הַגּוֹיִם
<M e>to give thanks to Your holy Name---
<M h> לְהוֹדוֹת לְשֵׁם קָדְשֶֽׁךָ,
<M e>to be extolled in Your praise.
<M h> לְהִשְׁתַּבֵּֽחַ בִּתְ֒הִלָּתֶֽךָ:
<xx><M tex><M e>Blessed is Adonoy, God of Israel
<M h> בָּרוּךְ יְהוָֹה אֱלֹהֵי יִשְׂרָאֵל,
<M e>from the world till the next world
<M h> מִן-הָֽעוֹלָם וְעַד הָֽעוֹלָם,
<M e>and all the people said: "Amen, Praise God."
<M h> וְאָמַר כָּל-הָעָם אָמֵן, הַֽלְ֒לוּיָהּ:
<M e>Let every soul praise God.
<M h> כֹּל הַנְּ֒שָׁמָה תְּהַלֵּל יָהּ,
<M e>Praise God.
<M h> הַֽלְ֒לוּיָהּ:
<M t1>To the Chief Musician:
<M h> <M newbold> לַמְ֒נַצֵּֽחַ <M reg>
<M e>a Psalm with instrumental music, a song.
<M h> בִּנְ֒גִינֹת מִזְמוֹר שִׁיר:
<M e>[May] God favor us and bless us,
<M h> אֱלֹהִים יְחָנֵּֽנוּ וִיבָרְ֒כֵֽנוּ
<M e>[may He] cause His countenance to shine
<M h> יָאֵר פָּנָיו
<M e>among us <i>Selah</i>;
<M h> אִתָּֽנוּ סֶֽלָה:
<M e>[So] that Your way become known on earth,
<M h> לָדַֽעַת בָּאָֽרֶץ דַּרְכֶּֽךָ
<M e>[and] Your deliverance among all nations.
<M h> בְּכָל-גּוֹיִם יְשׁוּעָתֶֽךָ:

<M e>Nations will rejoice and sing

<@02>Baruch She’amar
<@02>ברוך שאמר

The <i> Taz </i> (Orach Chaim 51:1) states that this prayer was instituted by the "Men of the Great Assembly." The blessing contains eighty-seven words suggesting the numerical value of <M hh> פָּז <M ee> <i> poz, </i> refined gold. <FL>

<@02>Mizmor Lesodah
<@02>מזמור לתודה
<M ex><EM><EN>Psalm 100 was recited in the Temple only on those days when thank-offerings were offered on the Altar.It is therefore omitted on Shabbos, on Yom Tov, on the day before Yom Kippur, on the day before Pesach, and also on the intermediate days of Pesach, when only obligatory-offerings were offered.<FL>
<EM><EN>Our Sages declare (<i>Midrash Rabbah Tzav,</i> 9) "In the future, even though all things on earth will be in such an ideal state that there will be no more cause<FJ>
<M tex>for prayers and offerings, prayers of gratitude, and offerings of thanksgiving will nevertheless not cease."<FL>
<EM><EN>Ordinarily, when a person is saved from a fatal illness, is released from captivity, or returns from a risky journey, he pronounces the special blessing <i>Hagomeil</i> (see page 177). Our Sages, instituted psalm 100 in our daily prayers as an expression of thanks for the many unrecognized miracles God performs in our behalf every day.<FL>
<M in>The following Psalm is omitted on Shabbat, Festivals, the day before Pesach, Chol HaMoed, Pesach and the day before Yom Kippur.<FC>

<@02>Yehi Chevod
<@02>יהי כבוד
<M ex> <EM> <EN> This prayer, mentioned in <i> Maseches Sof’rim </i> 17:11 is a collection of 18 verses from <i> Psalms, Chronicles, </i> and <i> Proverbs, </i> in which the Divine Name ( <M hh> הויה <M ee> ) is mentioned 18 times. Great care should be taken to pronounce the "Name" with the utmost concentration, keeping in mind that He is the Supreme Master of all that exists. <FL>

<@02>Ashrei
<@02>אשרי
<M ex><EM><EN>Rav S.R. Hirsch writes that the six concluding chapters of the Book of Psalms are the most important gift of David’s Divinely-inspired hymns that Israel treasures so greatly. These six psalms, 145-150, are an essential component of our daily prayers. Our Sages attach much significance to Psalm 145 in particular, and stated: "Whoever recites ‘A praise by David’ three times a day is assuredly worthy of a share in the world to come" (<i>Maseches Berachos</i> 4b). When recited in prayer this psalm is always introduced with two verses from other Psalms (84:5 and 144:15). These verses contain the word fortunate three times, an allusion to this psalm being recited three times a day. These verses are so closely identified with Psalm 145 that it is commonly referred to as <i>Ashrei</i> (Fortunate).<FL>
<M t2>Fortunate are those who dwell

<M e>fortunate is the people

<M h> דּוֹר לְדוֹר <FL>
<M e>will praise Your works,
<M h> יְשַׁבַּח מַעֲשֶׂיךָ <FL>
<M e>and Your mighty acts they will declare.
<M h> וּגְ֒בוּרֹתֶֽיךָ יַגִּֽידוּ: <FL>
<M e>The splendor of Your glorious majesty,
<M h> הֲדַר כְּבוֹד הוֹדֶֽךָ <FL>

<M h> וְדִבְ֒רֵי נִפְלְ֒אֹתֶֽיךָ אָשִֽׂיחָה: <FL>

<M h> וֶעֱזוּז נוֹרְ֒אֹתֶֽיךָ יֹאמֵרוּ <FL>
<M e>and Your greatness I will recount.
<M h> וּגְ֒דֻלָּתְ֒ךָ אֲסַפְּ֒רֶֽנָּה: <FL>
<M e>Mention of Your bountifulness
<M h> זֵֽכֶר רַב-טוּבְ֒ךָ
<M e>they will express,
<M h> יַבִּֽיעוּ <FL>
<M e>and in Your righteousness joyfully exult.
<M h> וְצִדְ֒קָתְ֒ךָ יְרַנֵּֽנוּ: <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>Adonoy is gracious and merciful,<M tnt>
<M h> חַנּוּן וְרַחוּם יְהֹוָה <FL>

<M e>Adonoy is good to all,
<M h> טוֹב-יְהֹוָה לַכֹּל <FL>

<M h> וְרַחֲמָיו עַל-כָּל-מַעֲשָׂיו: <FL>
<M e>All Your works will thank You, Adonoy,
<M h> יוֹדֽוּךָ יְהֹוָה כָּל-מַעֲשֶֽׂיךָ <FL>
<M e>and Your pious ones will bless You.<M tnt>
<M h> וַחֲסִידֶֽיךָ יְבָרְ֒כֽוּכָה: <FL>

<M h> כְּבוֹד מַלְ֒כוּתְ֒ךָ

<M h> יֹאמֵרוּ <FL>

<M h> וּגְ֒בוּרָתְ֒ךָ יְדַבֵּֽרוּ: <FL>

<M e>and Your dominion is in every generation.
<M h> וּמֶמְשַׁלְתְּךָ בְּכָל-דּוֹר וָדֹר: <FL>

<M h> סוֹמֵךְ יְהֹוָה לְכָל-הַנֹּפְ֒לִים <FL>

<M h> וְזוֹקֵף לְכָל-הַכְּ֒פוּפִים: <FL>

<M h> פּוֹתֵֽחַ אֶת-יָדֶֽךָ <FL>
<M e>and satisfy the desire of every living being.
<M h> וּמַשְׂבִּֽיעַ לְכָל-חַי רָצוֹן: <FL>
<M e>Adonoy is just in all His ways
<M h> צַדִּיק יְהֹוָה בְּכָל-דְּרָכָיו <FL>

<M h> רְצוֹן-יְרֵאָיו יַעֲשֶׂה <FL>

<M h> שֵׁם קָדְשׁוֹ לְעוֹלָם וָעֶד: <FL>

<M h> וַאֲנַֽחְנוּ נְבָרֵךְ יָהּ <FL>

<M t2>Praise God!

<M h> יְהֹוָה פֹּקֵֽחַ עִוְ֒רִים <FL>

<M h> יְהֹוָה שֹׁמֵר אֶת-גֵּרִים <FL>

<M h> יְעוֹדֵד <FL>

<M t2>Praise God!
<M h> <M newbold> הַלְ֒לוּיָהּ <M reg> <FL>

<M h> כִּי-טוֹב זַמְּ֒רָה אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ, <FL>

<M h> כִּי-נָעִים נָאוָה תְהִלָּה: <FL>

<M h> בּוֹנֵה יְרוּשָׁלַֽםִ יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>the banished ones of Israel He will gather.

<M h> וּמְ֒חַבֵּשׁ לְעַצְּ֒בוֹתָם: <FL>

<M h> מוֹנֶה מִסְפָּר לַכּוֹכָבִים <FL>

<M h> לִתְבוּנָתוֹ אֵין מִסְפָּר: <FL>

<M h> מְעוֹדֵד עֲנָוִים יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>He casts down the wicked to the ground.
<M h> מַשְׁפִּיל רְשָׁעִים עֲדֵי-אָֽרֶץ: <FL>
<M e>Cry out to Adonoy in thanksgiving;
<M h> עֱנוּ לַיהוָֹה בְּתוֹדָה <FL>
<M e>sing to our God with the harp.<M tnt>
<M h> זַמְּ֒רוּ לֵאלֹהֵֽינוּ בְכִנּוֹר: <FL>
<M e>[He] Who covers the heaven with clouds,
<M h> הַמְ֒כַסֶּה שָׁמַֽיִם בְּעָבִים <FL>
<M e>Who prepares rain for the earth;
<M h> הַמֵּכִין לָאָֽרֶץ מָטָר <FL>
<M e>Who causes grass to grow upon the hills.
<M h> הַמַּצְמִֽיחַ הָרִים חָצִיר: <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>Who gives the animal its fodder;
<M h> נוֹתֵן לִבְ֒הֵמָה לַחְמָהּ <FL>
<M e>[also] to the young ravens which call.
<M h> לִבְ֒נֵי עֹרֵב אֲשֶׁר יִקְרָֽאוּ: <FL>
<M e>Not the power of the horse does He desire,
<M h> לֹא בִגְ֒בוּרַת הַסּוּס יֶחְפָּץ <FL>
<M e>nor the thighs of man does He want.<M tnt>
<M h> לֹא בְשׁוֹקֵי הָאִישׁ יִרְצֶה: <FL>

<M h> רוֹצֶה יְהֹוָה אֶת-יְרֵאָיו <FL>
<M e>those who hope for His kindliness.
<M h> אֶת-הַמְ֒יַחֲלִים לְחַסְדּוֹ: <FL>
<M e>Jerusalem, praise Adonoy;
<M h> שַׁבְּ֒חִי יְרוּשָׁלַֽםִ אֶת יְהֹוָה <FL>

<M h> כִּי-חִזַּק בְּרִיחֵי שְׁעָרָֽיִךְ <FL>

<M h> הַשָּׂם-גְּבוּלֵךְ שָׁלוֹם <FL>

<M h> חֵֽלֶב חִטִּים יַשְׂבִּיעֵךְ: <FL>
<M e>He dispatches His command earthward;
<M h> הַשֹּׁלֵֽחַ אִמְרָתוֹ אָֽרֶץ <FL>

<M h> עַד-מְהֵרָה יָרוּץ דְּבָרוֹ: <FL>

<M h> הַנֹּתֵן שֶֽׁלֶג כַּצָּֽמֶר <FL>

<M h> כְּפוֹר כָּאֵֽפֶר יְפַזֵּר: <FL>

<M h> מַשְׁלִיךְ קַרְחוֹ כְפִתִּים <FL>

<M h> יִשְׁלַח דְּבָרוֹ וְיַמְסֵם <FL>

<M h> לֹא עָֽשָׂה כֵן לְכָל-גּוֹי <FL>

<M h> הַלְ֒לוּיָהּ: <FL>
<M ex><EM><EN>In this psalm, David sings of the moment when all the world will be imbued with the knowledge of God’s all-embracing providence. All living creatures---from the infinite heights of heaven above (verses 1-7) down to the depths of the earth below (verses 7-12)---will join together in one great hymn of praise to their Creator, and acknowledge the uniqueness of Israel over all other nations.<FL>
<M t2>Praise God.
<M h> <M newbold> הַלְ֒לוּיָהּ <M reg> <FL>
<M e>Praise Adonoy from the sky;

<M e>Praise Him, all His angels;
<M h> הַלְ֒לֽוּהוּ כָּל-מַלְאָכָיו <FL>
<M e>Praise Him, all His hosts!
<M h> הַלְ֒לֽוּהוּ כָּל-צְבָאָיו: <FL>

<M h> הַלְ֒לֽוּהוּ שֶֽׁמֶשׁ וְיָרֵֽחַ <FL>
<M e>Praise Him, all the stars of light.

<M h> וְהַמַּֽיִם אֲשֶׁר מֵעַל הַשָּׁמָֽיִם: <FL>

<M h> אָמֵן וְאָמֵן: <FL>
<xx><M tex><M ex><EM><EN>The following selections are additions to the <i>Pesukei Dezimrah.</i> The custom of reciting them is mentioned as early as the Gaonic era, specifically by Rav Amram Gaon.<FL>
<EM><EN>The first four verses (<i>1 Chronicles</i> 29:10-13) relate David’s blessing to God, when he presented the gold, silver, and jewels he amassed for the construction of the Holy Temple. It was a day of great rejoicing as, following David’s example, the leaders and princes also presented generous gifts for the construction of the Temple.<FL>
<EM><EN>These verses were incorporated into our daily prayers because they speak so eloquently of God’s majesty, and of the Divine providence which is the source of the power, riches, might, and honor of all human beings.<FL>
<M in> The following until after <M hh> ישתבח <M ee> should be said standing. <FC>
<M t2>And David blessed Adonoy
<M h> <M newbold> וַיְ֒בָֽרֶךְ דָּוִיד <M reg> אֶת-יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>in the presence of all the assembly;
<M h> לְעֵינֵי כָּל-הַקָּהָל <FL>
<M e>and David said,
<M h> וַיֹּֽאמֶר דָּוִיד <FL>
<M e>Blessed are You, Adonoy,
<M h> בָּרוּךְ אַתָּה יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>God of Israel, our father,<M tnt>
<M h> אֱלֹהֵי יִשְׂרָאֵל אָבִֽינוּ, <FL>
<M e>forever and ever.
<M h> מֵעוֹלָם וְעַד-עוֹלָם: <FL>
<M e>Yours, Adonoy,
<M h> לְךָ יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>is the greatness, the might, the glory
<M h> הַגְּ֒דֻלָּה וְהַגְּ֒בוּרָה וְהַתִּפְאֶֽרֶת <FL>
<M e>the victory and the beauty,<M tnt>
<M h> וְהַנֵּֽצַח וְהַהוֹד <FL>
<M e>for all that is in heaven and on earth
<M h> כִּי-כֹל בַּשָּׁמַֽיִם וּבָאָֽרֶץ <FL>
<M e>[is Yours]; Yours, Adonoy, is the kingdom
<M h> לְךָ יְהֹוָה הַמַּמְלָכָה <FL>
<M e>and You are uplifted,
<M h> וְהַמִּתְנַשֵּׂא <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>[supreme] over all rulers.
<M h> לְכֹל לְרֹאשׁ: <FL>
<M e>The riches and the honor come from You,
<M h> וְהָעֽשֶׁר וְהַכָּבוֹד מִלְּ֒פָנֶֽיךָ <FL>
<M e>and You rule over all;
<M h> וְאַתָּה מוֹשֵׁל בַּכֹּל, <FL>
<M e>in Your hand are power and might,
<M h> וּבְיָדְ֒ךָ כֹּֽחַ וּגְ֒בוּרָה, <FL>
<M e>and [it is] in Your hand
<M h> וּבְ֒יָדְ֒ךָ <FL>
<M e>to bestow greatness and strength upon all.
<M h> לְגַדֵּל וּלְ֒חַזֵּק לַכֹּל: <FL>
<M e>And now, our God,
<M h> וְעַתָּה אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ <FL>
<M e>we give thanks to You
<M h> מוֹדִים אֲנַֽחְנוּ לָךְ <FL>
<M e>and praise Your glorious Name.<M tnt>
<M h> וּמְ֒הַלְ֒לִים לְשֵׁם תִּפְאַרְתֶּֽךָ: <FL>
<M ex><EM><EN>The next six verses are taken from <i>Nehemiah</i> 9:6-11. They are the last words of praise found in Scripture.<FL>
<M t2>You alone are Adonoy;<M tnt>

<M h> וְאֶת-רֹדְ֒פֵיהֶם <FL>
<M e>You hurled into the depths,
<M h> הִשְׁלַֽכְתָּ בִמְצוֹלֹת <FL>
<M e>like a stone into mighty waters.<M tnt>
<M h> כְּמוֹ-אֶֽבֶן בְּמַֽיִם עַזִּים: <FL>
<@02>Shiras Hayam
<@02>שירת הים
<M ex><EM><EN>In Temple times Shiras Hayam, the Song of the Sea, was sung by the Levites when the daily afternoon sacrifice was offered.<M tnt> After the destruction, the Jews of the Holy Land continued the tradition, reciting the Shira at the end of the <i>Pesukei<i> Dezimrah.</i> The custom spread to Italy and from there to other Jewish communities. This daily recital is mentioned by Rav Saadya Gaon but not as an obligatory part of the service. Rambam calls it a "custom."<M tnt> Subsequently adopted by all communities, reciting the Shira became an integral part of our daily prayers.<FL>
<EM><EN>Some hold that the Shira should be chanted aloud while standing. It should be sung with joy as at the time of the Exodus. <i>"Sheloh"</i> writes that reciting the Shira atones for sin, so that if one wishes to repent a serious sin, he should recite the Shira every day with great fervor. The <i>Zohar</i> says, "If one recites this song with elation and joy, he will be worthy to sing it in the next world. He will also be worthy to sing it when he greets the Messiah."<FL>
<M t2>On that day,<M tnt> Adonoy delivered
<M h> <M newbold> וַיּֽוֹשַׁע יְהֹוָה <M reg> בַּיּוֹם הַהוּא <FL>
<M e>Israel from the hand of Egypt,
<M h> אֶת-יִשְׂרָאֵל מִיַּד מִצְרָֽיִם <FL>
<M e>and Israel saw the Egyptians
<M h> וַיַּרְא יִשְׂרָאֵל אֶת-מִצְרַֽיִם <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>dead on the seashore.
<M h> מֵת עַל-שְׂפַת הַיָּם: <FL>
<M e>And Israel saw the great hand<M tnt>
<M h> <M chaz> וַיַּרְא יִשְׂרָאֵל אֶת-הַיָּד הַגְּ֒דֹלָה <FL>
<M e>which Adonoy wielded against Egypt,
<M h> אֲשֶׁר עָשָׂה יְהֹוָה בְּמִצְרַֽיִם <FL>
<M e>and the people feared Adonoy,
<M h> וַיִּירְ֒אוּ הָעָם אֶת יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>and they believed in Adonoy,
<M h> וַיַּאֲמִֽינוּ בַּיהוָֹה <FL>
<M e>and that Moses was His servant.
<M h> וּבְ֒משֶׁה עַבְדּוֹ: <FL>
<M e><M t1>Then Moses and the Children of Israel sang

<M e>was the cause of my deliverance;<M tnt>
<M h> וַיְ֒הִי-לִי לִישׁוּעָה <FL>

<M in>During the Ten Days of Penitence add:<FC>
<M ex>In this Psalm, said during the Ten Days of Penitence, the Jewish soul sings of the Jewish spirit ascending from the depths of the deepest misery of all, the burden of sin and guilt.<FL>
<M ts>A Song of Ascents.
<M h> <b> שִׁיר הַמַּעֲלוֹת </b> <FL>
<M es>Out of the depths
<M hs> מִמַּעֲמַקִּים <FL>
<M es>I have called to You, Adonoy.
<M hs> קְרָאתִֽיךָ יְהֹוָה: <FL>
<M es>My Master, hear my voice;
<M hs> אֲדֹנָי שִׁמְ֒עָה בְקוֹלִי <FL>
<M es>let Your ears be attentive
<M hs> תִּהְיֶֽינָה אָזְנֶֽיךָ קַשֻּׁבוֹת <FL>
<M es>to the voice of my supplications.
<M hs> לְקוֹל תַּחֲנוּנָי: <FL>
<M es>If You God should take account of iniquities,
<M hs> אִם-עֲוֹנוֹת תִּשְׁמָר-יָהּ <FL>
<M es>my Master, who could survive?
<M hs> אֲדֹנָי מִי יַעֲמֹד: <FL>
<M es>For with You is forgiveness,
<M hs> כִּי-עִמְּ֒ךָ הַסְּ֒לִיחָה <FL>

<M es>[more than] the watchman [waits]
<M hs> שֹׁמְ֒רִים <FL>

<M hs> מִכֹּל עֲוֹנוֹתָיו: <FL>
<M tex><M in>The Half-Kaddish is recited by the </i>Chazzan<FC>
<M ex><EM><EN>Here, as elsewhere in the Liturgy, the Half-Kaddish marks the end of a distinct section of the prayers, in this case, the <i>Pesukei Dezimrah.</i><FL>
<EM><EN>It is called the Half-Kaddish, the final three verses of the complete Kaddish having been omitted.<FL>

<SZ 11><zl>S<SZ 8>HACHARIS<SZ 11>S<SZ 8>ERVICE<SZ 11><FC></hdr><hdr o><inx><ib 1><FT stn><SZ 12><pa><FL>
<SZ 11><zl>S<SZ 8>HACHARIS<SZ 11>S<SZ 8>ERVICE<SZ 11><FC></hdr>
<pb><M tex><M ex><EM><EN>It has become a universally-accepted custom to recite <i>Barechu</i> before proceeding to the blessings of <i>Shema. Barechu,</i> like <i>Kaddish</i> and <i>Kedushah,</i> cannot be recited unless a quorum---a <i>minyan</i> of ten adult males---is present. <i>Barechu</i> is also said by one who is called upon to read from the Torah.<FL>
<EM><EN>The practice of saying <i>Barechu</i> is mentioned numerous times in the Talmud. It is even cited in the Mishna (<i>Maseches Berachos</i> 49b) in the names of Rabbi Akiva and Rabbi Yishmael.<FL>
<M in>The </i>Chazzan<i> says:<FC>
<M t2>Bless Adonoy Who is blessed.
<M h> <M newbold> בָּרְ֒כוּ <M reg> אֶת יְהֹוָה הַמְּ֒בֹרָךְ: <FL>
<M in>The Congregation responds and the </i>Chazzan<i> repeats:<FC>
<M t2>Blessed is Adonoy, Who is blessed
<M h> <M newbold> בָּרוּךְ <M reg> יְהֹוָה הַמְּ֒בֹרָךְ <FL>
<M e>forever and ever.
<M h> לְעוֹלָם וָעֶד: <FL>
<@02>The Blessings of Shema
<@02>ברכות קריאת שמע
<M ex> <EM> <EN> The two blessings <M hh> יוֹצֵר אוֹר <M ee> "He Who forms light" and <M hh> אַהֲבָה רַבָּה <M ee> "Great love," are referred to as the blessings preceding Shema ( <i> Maseches Berachos </i> 11a). According to Rambam they were formulated by Ezra and his Court ( <i> Laws of Shema </i> 1:7). <FL>
<EM> <EN> You may not interrupt your prayers from this point on until after the <i> Shemoneh Esrei </i> . But you may answer "Amein" to the blessings of <M hh> הָאֵל הַקָּדוֹשׁ <M ee> "The holy Powerful One" and <M hh> שׁוֹמֵעַ תְּפִילָּה <M ee> "He Who heeds prayer;" say the thrice-repeated <M hh> קָדוֹשׁ <M ee> "Holy <NS> . <NS> . <NS> ." and <M hh> בָּרוּךְ כְּבוֹד <M ee> "Blessed is the glory <NS> . <NS> . <NS> ." of <i> Kedushah </i> ; and answer <i> Barechu. </i> You may also answer <M hh> אָמֵן יְהֵא שְׁמֵהּ רַבָּא <M ee> "Amein, May His great Name," when you hear Kaddish." You may also answer Amein after the blessings of <M hh> יוֹצֵר הַמְּאוֹרוֹת <M ee> , "Who forms the luminaries," and <M hh> הַבּוֹחֵר בְּעַמּוֹ יִשְׂרָאֵל בְּאַהֲבָה <M ee> , "Who chooses His people Israel with love." <FL>
<EM><EN>For a more detailed exposition of these laws, see <i>Metsudah Kitzur Shulchan Aruch,</i> Vol. I, pp. 172-176.<FL>

<M ex><EM><EN>In the second of the blessings that precede <i>Shema</i> we praise God for His goodness in giving us His Torah, and pray for His help in the study of Torah. None of our petitions for the material goods of life approaches the fervor of this prayer for knowledge of the Torah and steadfastness in obeying it.<FL>

<@02>Recitation of Shema
<@02>קריאת שמע
<M ex><EM><EN>The recitation of Shema was part of the daily worship in the Holy Temple, and our Sages ordained that it be recited in the synagogue service, providing it a central place in the morning and evening prayers of each Jew. Its importance may be judged from the fact that the very first Mishnah in the Oral Torah opens with the question, "From what time may the evening Shema be read?"<FL>
<EM> <EN> In reading Shema, bear in mind that you are performing a Scriptural commandment. All three paragraphs should be read with <i> kavanah, </i> concentrated intention, on what you are saying. The entire Shema should be recited in awe and reverence as it proclaims the existence and unity of God; the Jews’ complete dedication to God and His commandments; the belief in Divine justice; the remembrance of the Exodus and the selection of the Jews as God’s Chosen People. These concepts are the pillars of the Jewish faith. Whenever this sign ( <dc 235> ) appears (e.g. <M hh> בְּכָל-לְבָבְ֒ךָ <M ee> ), it indicates that you should be careful to pronounce each word distinctly. In many instances, the last letter of the first word and first letter of the second word are the same, the words might be read as one, which is not the proper way to fulfill the mitzvah of Kerias Shema. <FL>
<xx><M tex><M in>The following three words should be said when praying without a </i>minyan</i>:<FC>
<M t2>(Almighty, faithful King)

<M ex> <EM> <EN> You must be careful to connect the last words of Shema, <M hh> ה' אֱלֺקֵיכֶם <M ee> (Adonoy, your God), with the word <M hh> אמת <M ee> (is true) without pause or interruption so that these three words form one sentence, meaning "Adonoy your God is true" ( <i> Maseches <i> Berachos </i> 13a). <FL>

<xx> <M tex> <M ex> <EM> <EN> The following prayer, which culminates with <M hh> גָאַל יִשְׂרָאַל <M ee> , Who redeemed Israel, constitutes the "Blessing after Shema" mentioned in the Talmud ( <i> Maseches Berachos </i> 11a). It is also mentioned in <i> Maseches Tamid </i> (32b) as part of the morning service in the Temple. <FL>

<M h> וְאָמְ֒רוּ כֻלָּם: <FL>
<M e><M t1>"Who is like You among the mighty, Adonoy!
<M h> מִי כָמֹֽכָה בָּאֵלִם יְהֹוָה <FL>
<M e>Who is like You---
<M h> מִי כָּמֹֽכָה <FL>

<M h> נֶאְדָּר בַּקֹּֽדֶשׁ <FL>
<M e>awesome in praise, performing wonders!"
<M h> נוֹרָא תְהִלֹּת עֹֽשֵׂה פֶֽלֶא: <FL>
<M e><M t1>With a new song the redeemed people praised
<M h> שִׁירָה חֲדָשָׁה שִׁבְּ֒חוּ גְאוּלִים <FL>
<M e>Your great Name at the seashore!
<M h> לְשִׁמְךָ הַגָּדוֹל עַל שְׂפַת הַיָּם <FL>

<M h> יַֽחַד כֻּלָּם <FL>
<M e>gave thanks
<M h> הוֹדוּ
<M e>and proclaimed Your sovereignty,
<M h> וְהִמְלִֽיכוּ <FL>
<M e>and said:
<M h> וְאָמְרוּ: <FL>
<M e>"Adonoy will reign forever and ever."

<M h> קֽוּמָה בְּעֶזְרַת יִשְׂרָאֵל <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>and liberate
<M h> וּפְ֒דֵה <FL>

﻿<VER Kivun Ltd. Dagesh Professional/PC, Version 0.98U><MACROFILE G.DGM><M 00><bpn 131><hdr e><inx><ib 1><FT stn><SZ 12><pa><FR>
<SZ 11><zl>S<SZ 8>HACHARIS<SZ 11>S<SZ 8>ERVICE<SZ 11><FC></hdr><hdr o><inx><ib 1><FT stn><SZ 12><pa><FL>
<SZ 11><zl>S<SZ 8>HACHARIS<SZ 11>S<SZ 8>ERVICE<SZ 11><FC></hdr>
<pb><M ex>Fundamentals of <i>Kuzari,</i> (Metsudah Publications, 1979) pages 269, 271, 273.<FL>
<EM><EN>When reciting <i>Shemoneh Esrei,</i> you must adhere to these rules:<FL>
<EM><EN>1.<fs>Before beginning the prayer, take three steps backwards and then return to your former position. Upon completing the prayer, take three steps backwards and return.<FL>
<EM><EN>2.<fs>Keep your feet together.<FL>
<EM><EN>3.<fs>Concentrate on the meaning of the words you are uttering. Remove all distracting thoughts and worries from your mind.<FL>
<EM><EN>4.<fs>You may not interrupt <i>Shemoneh Esrei</i> by talking, not even by answering Amein. If you should hear <i>Kedushah, Kaddish,</i> or <i>Barechu</i> while saying the <i>Shemoneh Esrei,</i> you should remain silent and listen to the Chazzan’s words.<FL>
<EM><EN>5.<fs>At the beginning and end of the first blessing, at the beginning and end of the blessing that begins: "We are thankful to You," (page 133) and ends with "The Beneficent is Your Name," (page 140) we half-kneel and bow in the following manner: At the word "Blessed," bend your knees; at the word "You," bend forward until the vertebrae of your spinal cord are loosened; at "Adonoy," return to your upright position in keeping with the verse, "Adonoy straightens the bent" (<i>Psalms</i> 146:8).<FL>
<EM><EN>6.<fs>Each individual recites <i>Shemoneh Esrei</i> in silence. Only the prayer leader, the <i>Chazzan,</i> ever recites it aloud, and then only after the entire congregation, himself included, has recited it silently.<FL>

<M t1>My Master,<M tnt> open my lips,

<M t2><M sc>PRAYER FOR RETURN OF DIVINE SERVICE
<M h> עבודה <FR>
<M e>Be pleased,<M tnt> Adonoy, our God,
<M h> רְצֵה יְהֹוָה אֱלֹהֵֽינוּ <FL>
<M e>with Your people Israel
<M h> בְּעַמְּ֒ךָ יִשְׂרָאֵל
<M e>and pay need to their prayer;<M tnt>
<M h> וְלִתְ֒פִלָּתָם שְׁעֵה, <FL>
<M e>and restore the service
<M h> וְהָשֵׁב אֶת הָעֲבוֹדָה <FL>
<M e>to the Holy of Holies in Your abode,
<M h> לִדְ֒בִיר בֵּיתֶֽךָ <FL>
<M e>and the fire-offerings<M tnt> of Israel;
<M h> וְאִשֵּׁי יִשְׂרָאֵל, <FL>
<M e>and accept their prayer, lovingly
<M h> וּתְ֒פִלָּתָם בְּאַהֲבָה תְקַבֵּל
<M e>and willingly.
<M h> בְּרָצוֹן <FL>
<xx><M tex><M e>And may You always find pleasure
<M h> וּתְ֒הִי לְרָצוֹן תָּמִיד <FL>
<M e>with the service of Your people, Israel.

<M ex> <EM> <EN> If you forgot to say this at Shacharis, (the Morning Service) or at Mincha (the Afternoon Service), but realized your omission before saying <M hh> מוֹדִים <M ee> , "We are thankful," you should say it at that time and continue with <M hh> מוֹדִים <M ee> . <FL>
<EM> <EN> If you became aware of your omission after saying " <M hh> מוֹדִים <M ee> " "We are thankful," but before concluding the Shemoneh Esrei [and taking three steps backwards], start again from <M hh> רְצֵה <M ee> , "Be pleased." If you had completed the Shemoneh Esrei and then remembered, you must repeat the <i> entire </i> Shemoneh Esrei from the beginning. <FL>
<EM><EN>If you are in doubt, follow the same procedure as above.<FL>
<EM> <EN> If you had already said the Musaf prayer and recalled your omission, it is the opinion of some authorities, that the <i> Shemoneh Esrei of Shacharis </i> be repeated as a <M hh> נְדָבָה <M ee> , a free-will-offering of prayer, rather than an obligatory prayer. <FC>

<@02>Tachanun
<@02>תחנון
<M in>On Rosh Chodesh, Chol HaMoed, and Chanukah, Hallel is recited. See page 000.<FC>
<AF 6>On Fast Days (Monday---Thursday---Monday, Tenth of Teves, Fast of Esther, Seventeenth of Tamuz) </i>Selichos<i> are recited. See pages 000<k 2>ff.<FC>
<AF 6>On days when </i>Tachanun<i> is omitted (see below) the chazzan continues with Half Kaddish on page 000.<FC>

﻿<VER Kivun Ltd. Dagesh Professional/PC, Version 0.98U><MACROFILE G.DGM><M 00><bpn 161><hdr e><inx><ib 1><FT stn><SZ 12><pa><FR>
<SZ 11><zl>S<SZ 8>HACHARIS<SZ 11> S<SZ 8>ERVICE<SZ 11><FC></hdr><hdr o><inx><ib 1><FT stn><SZ 12><pa><FL>
<SZ 11><zl>S<SZ 8>HACHARIS<SZ 11> S<SZ 8>ERVICE<SZ 11><FC></hdr>
<pb><M ex>(14 and 15 Adar Rishon in a leap year); the entire month of Nissan; Pesach Sheini (14 Iyar); Lag BaOmer; 1-8 Sivan; 9 and 15 Av; and 29 Elul. When <i>Tachanun</i> is omitted on these days, it is also omitted at the preceding Mincha (afternoon service).<FL>
<EM><EN><i>Tachanun</i> is also omitted in the presence of a bridegroom, in the house of a mourner during the week of mourning, and on the occasion of a circumcision if the father, the <i>sandak</i> or the <i>mohel</i> is present. The worshipper recites the <i>Tachanun</i> in a sitting position, while resting his brow on his arm. During the morning service, when the hand-<i>tefillin</i> is on the left arm, he leans his brow on his right arm, but at the Mincha service he leans his brow on his left arm. This "falling on one’s face" symbolizes complete submission to God and the committing of our destinies into His hands. It is mentioned in the Talmud (<i>Maseches Megillah</i> 22b), and originates with Moses, who "Fell down before God" (<i>Deuteronomy</i> 9:18) and was followed by Joshua, who "Fell on the earth upon his face before the Ark of God" (<k 2><i>Joshua</i> 7:6)<FL>
<M t2>Our God and God of our fathers,
<M h> <M reg> אֱלֺהֵֽינוּ וֵאלֺהֵי אֲבוֹתֵֽינוּ

<@02>Avinu Malkeinu
<@02>אבינו מלכנו
<M ex><EM><EN>During the Ten Days of Penitence, <i>Avinu Malkeinu</i> is recited here during <i>Shacharis</i>---the morning service, and <i>Mincha</i>---the afternoon service. It is also said by some congregations on public Fast Days. The number of petitions in this prayer varies with custom, but in our rite, <i>Avinu Malkeinu</i> consists of 44 petitions. Since many of them are similar to the petitions of <i>Shemoneh Esrei, Avinu Malkeinu</i> is never recited on Shabbos, when the petitions of <i>Shemoneh Esrei</i> are also omitted.<FL>
<EM><EN>This unique and moving prayer is recorded as having been recited by Rabbi Akiva. The Talmud (<i>Maseches Taanis</i> 25b) relates that Rabbi Eliezer once stepped down before the Ark and recited the 24 benedictions for fast days and his prayers were not answered. Rabbi Akiva stepped down after him and exclaimed, "Our Father, our King, we have no king except You. Our Father, our King, for Your sake have mercy on us," and rain fell.<FL>

<M h> <M newbold> אָבִֽינוּ מַלְכֵּֽנוּ <M reg>

<xx><M tex><M e>we have no King except You.<M tnt>

<M h> אָבִֽינוּ מַלְכֵּֽנוּ

<M e>and deliver us.
<M h> וְהוֹשִׁיעֵֽנוּ:
<@02>Vehu Rachum
<@02>והוא רחום
<M e><M in>The following prayers are added on Mondays and Thursday:<FC>
<EM>On other days, continue "Guardian of Israel. . .," on page 000:<FC>
<M ex><EM><EN>This group of somber plaints, known as the "long <i>Vehu Rachum</i>" is recited in the morning service on Mondays and Thursdays, except on days when <i>Tachanun</i> is omitted.<FL>
<EM><EN>The origin of these seven prayers is shrouded in legend. It has been suggested that they were composed during the terrible persecutions at the hands of the Goths in seventh-century Spain. It has been said, "Whoever can read this ‘long <i>Vehu Rachum</i>’ prayer without emotion has lost all feeling for what is great and noble."<FL>
<EM><EN>Despite all the repetition in these cries for forgiveness, mercy, help, and protection, the effect is not tiring; because here it is not merely an individual soul, but the soul of an entire people that utters these laments and supplications, that gives voice to this woe of nearly two thousand years.<FL>
<EM><EN>Moses ascended Mount Sinai to receive the Second Tablets on the fifth day of the week, and he returned to the people on the second day of the week, bringing them the new tablets as a security for the Divine covenant and as confirmation of God’s atonement for their transgression. Ever since,<FJ>
<EM>the second and fifth day of each week, Monday and Thursday, have been days of summons to the Jewish people to assemble anew before God and to reaffirm their sincere "return" to the Law of God. Our regular service is therefore augmented on these days by these additional supplications.<FL>
<M t2>And He, the merciful One,
<M h> <M newbold> וְהוּא רַחוּם <M reg>
<M e>will atone iniquity, and will not destroy,
<M h> יְכַפֵּר עָוֺן וְלֹא-יַשְׁחִית
<M e>He frequently withdraws His anger,
<M h> וְהִרְבָּה לְהָשִׁיב אַפּוֹ
<M e>and does not arouse all His rage.<M tnt>
<M h> וְלֹא-יָעִיר כָּל-חֲמָתוֹ:
<M e>You, Adonoy,
<M h> אַתָּה יְהֹוָה
<M e>do not withhold Your mercy from us;

<M h> כִּי רַחוּם אָֽתָּה:
<M e>for such is Your way---
<M h> כִּי כֵן דַּרְכֶּֽךָ
<M e>to bestow undeserved kindness
<M h> עֹשֶׂה חֶֽסֶד חִנָּם

<M h> בְּכָל-דּוֹר וָדוֹר:

<M h> חֽוּסָה יְהֹוָה עַל-עַמֶּֽךָ
<M e>and save us from Your wrath;
<M h> וְהַצִּילֵֽנוּ מִזַּעְמֶֽךָ:
<M e>remove from us the scourge of plague,
<M h> וְהָסֵר מִמֶּֽנּוּ מַכַּת הַמַּגֵּפָה
<M e>and harsh decree,
<M h> וּגְ֒זֵרָה קָשָׁה
<M e>for You are the Guardian of Israel.
<M h> כִּי אַתָּה שׁוֹמֵר יִשְׂרָאֵל:
<M e>Righteousness is Yours, my Master,

<M e>while shame is ours.<M tnt>
<M h> וְלָֽנוּ בּֽשֶׁת הַפָּנִים:
<M e>How can we complain?
<M h> מַה-נִּתְאוֹנֵן
<M e>What can we say?
<M h> וּמַה-נֹּאמַר
<M e>What can we speak?
<M h> מַה-נְּדַבֵּר
<M e>and how can we justify ourselves?
<M h> וּמַה-נִּצְטַּדָּק:

<M e>to receive those who repent.
<M h> לְקַבֵּל שָׁבִים:

<M h> אָֽנָּא יְהֹוָה
